This book is completed for you, O my sons, it is a part of the knowledge of medicine, fully detailed and reaching its goal in clarity and explanation. I thought it fitting to complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the manual of surgery.
The practice of surgery in our land and time is poor due to the lack of doctors, causing the art to be neglected and its effects reduced. The only remnants of surgery in ancient texts are simple diagrams, engraved by hands and filled with error and confusion, until their meanings were lost and their benefits disappeared.
I intend to revive and enrich this field with this treatise through explanation, clarification, conciseness, and providing illustrations of the human body and other tools used in surgery, as it is a means of adding detail and facilitating what is necessary.
The reason that there is no skilled craftsman in our time is because the practice of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its practitioner to study the art of dissection as described by Galenus before engaging in it. One should understand the functions of the limbs and their joints, connections and disconnections, knowledge of bones and nerves, their number, exits, arteries, veins, and pulse points, as well as the locations of their exits and origins.
Physicians are plentiful in name but few in action, and certainly not skilled in the art of surgery. We have mentioned some of them at the beginning of this book.
Those who are not well-versed in what we have mentioned regarding surgery will inevitably make mistakes that lead to the death of people, as you have often seen many who claim knowledge and expertise in this field without actual understanding or experience.
This is why I have seen an ignorant doctor cut on the neck of a woman with a pigs' tooth, breaking some veins in her neck; blood gushed out until she died between his hands.
You will also see another doctor attempting to remove a stone from a man who had been bitten by it in the eye, and the stone was large; it was crushed before being removed with a piece of glass. The man died after about three days, and I had advised him to have it removed; however, you can see from the bone of the stone and the surrounding condition that this could not have been done.
You will also see another doctor who lived off the leaders of our country on medicine.
A blacksmith once had a fracture near his heel with an injury; the ignorant doctor hastily treated it by setting the fracture on the injury with great force and certainty, and left no chance for the injury to heal.
Then release it on its desires, then leave it for some days and command it not to suture until it twitches his leg and foot and excel in healing.
Bring it (the patient) and hasten the suturing, so that comfort is achieved and he is released from his ailment, except that corruption has already ruled the limb and I could not cure it.
Corruption continues to strive in the limb until it perishes.
You see a later doctor, pale and weak with cancer, then he dies after days until his bones crumble, and this is because if cancer has become malignant from mixing of black substances, it is not appropriate to expose it to iron pincers.
Except that it is in a limb capable of being excised completely.
Therefore, my sons, it is necessary for you to know that work with hands divides into two: a work accompanied by safety and a work with pain in most cases.
And beware of every work that comes from this book which has fear and danger, so it is necessary for you to avoid it and refuse it.
Lest the ignorant find his way to speech and slander, take for yourselves belts and garments and treat your patients with kindness and firmness.
Apply the best method leading to safety and praiseworthy outcome, examine the dangerous and intricate ailments thoroughly.
Protect yourselves from what you fear may mislead you in your religion and worldly life, for it will remain a barrier to your path and elevate you in the world and the hereafter according to your abilities.
According to Galen in some of his advice, do not treat an illness poorly lest you be known as a poor physician.
This article is divided into three sections.
The first part.
In the first part, about burning with fire and cutting with sharp instruments arranged from head to toe and tools images and all that is required by hand in work.
The second part.
In incisions, lacerations, fractures, suturing, amputation, and extraction of foreign bodies, etc., all these in orderly sequence accompanied by illustrations of instruments.
Chapter Three.
In algebra, calculus, treatment of wounds and similar matters arranged from head to foot, accompanied by illustrations of instruments.
Chapter One.
On the Knee.
Before describing the work on it, it is necessary to mention its advantages and disadvantages, and under what condition it should be used.
I say that the discussion on the advantages and disadvantages of the knee, a detailed and precise science, is secret knowledge known by some scholars.
They have differed on it and its explanation has been shortened out of fear of elongation.
I say that the knee is beneficial in general for all bad conditions of joints, whether with or without substance, and these are two types: the hot joint without substance and the dry joint without substance.
As for the dry joint with substance, they have differed on it. Some say that the knee is beneficial in this case, while others disagree and say that the knee does not help in a disease that is both hot and dry because the nature of heat and dryness are similar.
Among the ailments is treating a cold and dry warm disease, or a hot and dry cold one. The one who says contrary to that, states that charcoal in fire may benefit from a cold and dry warm disease occurring in human bodies. Whenever you insert charcoal into the human body and moisten it to a state of heat, you will cool down the human body.
I say with his (Albucasis's) words, because experience has shown me this fact numerous times, except that it should not be relied upon unless one has studied and trained in the field of charcoal making, specifically in the art of making quality charcoal. The diversity of the constitutions of people, their diseases, their causes, their symptoms, and their duration should be considered.
As for other types of constitutions, there is no fear of them for you, and the cold moist diseases have reached a consensus among physicians, and they do not differ regarding the benefit of charcoal in such diseases.
Know, oh sons, that the secret of treating with charcoal by fire and its superiority over charred medicines is that fire has a unique property that only affects the affected part without harming another connected part, except for a mild damage.
If the [medicine] that burns is applied to a member beyond what follows, it may encounter resistance from other parts and possibly cause disease in the member, perhaps even death. Fire, because of its nobility and honor, does not do this unless it persists.
It has become clear to us through experience, the duration of service, attention to craftsmanship, and adherence to facts.
I have refrained from lengthy speech, but if it does not belong in this book, I would have informed you of the secret and effective way to make fire destroy diseases in the body through a philosophical argument that will clarify your understanding.
Know, O sons, that they have differed regarding the time when the [medicine] is effective and considered the best time as spring.
I say that the [medicine] can be effective in any time because the harm that precedes time takes a while to achieve the benefit that is brought by the [medicine]. And certainly, if the [medicine] is of vital necessity that does not allow delay, fear of it following in its wake is greater than the danger from what precedes time.
Do not perform on you, O sons, what the common people and the ignorance of physicians may suspect, namely: something that does not require recurrence, and make it a habit.
This operation is not to be performed, as you believe that this thing is only like a medicine which changes the complexion and dries the humors that are the cause of the diseases.
This thing is superior to the medicine in terms of quick success, effectiveness, and intensity of its action.
The disease may return at some time due to the nature of its cause, enabling it and strengthening it, and what cannot be expected in the body from the gathering of impurities within it and the preoccupation of the soul with acquiring food and similar reasons.
O Allah, may the disease that is used in it (the operation) be a gentle disease and in a little impure part or humors. Similar to the extraction of a tooth from pain and similar things, it may not return in that place and this will be in the least degree.
And as for the common people's saying that this thing is the last of medicine, it is a true statement to the extent that those who say so believe that there is no remedy that can be beneficial with medicine or without it after the operation and prescription contrary to that.
The meaning is that the last of healing (therapy) is when we use the doses of treatment in a disease, and those medicines did not work, then we use another therapy and it worked. Therefore, from here it is clear that the last of healing (therapy) is the last of medicine. The meaning is that, generally and among many ignorant doctors, it has become widely known.
It has been mentioned at the beginning that gold is better than iron, and they say so because of the nobility and shine of gold. However, they are mistaken in thinking that the location of the therapy (kunya) depends on this. This is not correct in general.
I have tried this, and found that it works only in some animals, not others. The therapy (kunya) with gold is better and more effective than iron as they say; but if you protect the pot with gold in fire, it does not indicate when it will be protected up to the degree of redness of gold.
And because it speeds up the cold and if you increase its protection in fire, it melts quickly in the pot. Therefore, the therapist among us prefers iron over gold for efficiency; may Allah help him do the right thing.
This chapter is arranged in order from the head to the foot, so that it may be easy for the student, if Allah wills, what he desires from it.
The First Chapter.
In the head, there is one method (or technique).
This method (or technique) is beneficial against excessive moisture and dryness on the skull, which are causes of headache, frequent discharges from the head to the sides of the eyes and ears, frequent sleepiness and toothaches and other scalp wounds. In general, for every disease that results from dryness, such as scabs, headache, scalp itch, and similar diseases.
This picture commands the patient first to rinse his head with an easy-to-use, gentle shampoo for three or four nights according to the strength and habit of the patient.
Then he commands him to cut his hair with scissors, then he sits him between your hands with his hands on his chest.
Then you put the palm of your hand on his windpipe between his eyes, then when your middle finger reaches its end, teach this position with a movement (or gesture).
Then heat the olive oil bottle shown in this picture.
Expose from the bone the size of a walnut or an almond. Raise your hand if it is not, otherwise prepare your hand with iron again, or with something else if you have grown cold. Expose from the bone as you mentioned, then take some salt and put it in water and drink a small amount of it. Place it on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then place a soaked cloth (in oil) on it and leave it until the dryness of the burn goes away, then treat it with the four-finger-width ointment until it heals, if God wills.
They said that a wound, whenever it remains open, causes putrefaction and it is better and more beneficial.
Some of them mentioned that the skin should be pulled to the bone and the stitch kept until part of the bone marrow burns, then it is crushed afterwards, what burned from the bone is removed, then it is treated.
Others said that it should be stretched until it affects the bone in a strong way, so that a piece of the bone falls out like a chip or a small flake, and they claimed that this is beneficial for the healing of the skull and leaving the wound open for a long time.
Then he treats it until it breaks, and I do not see these two types of fractures except in some people and on the way to breakage and leave them for better and with safety if it is present; indeed, the head swells when its natural connection separates, as we have seen in other members.
Indeed, when the humerus head is naturally weak and the first type of fracture submits and is better for me, I use it and do it if Allah wills.
The Second Chapter.
Fractures of the head (also).
If a fracture occurs in the neck of the humerus and it is long, then use traction, compression, pulling, bandages and padding; indeed, if the fractured bone has been set, nothing of that will be helpful, observe. If the head of the humerus is strong by nature and not weak, and it found a hard splint, then break another bone slightly above it. Then break a bone on every joint of the head until the skin separates and reveals the muscle layer that we have described. Apply a probe deeply at the site known as 'the fauces' and gently with your hand in this position, do not dislocate the bone, for it will cause her intense pain unlike other skull fractures. I shall refer to this specific fracture in its location.
It is important to perform a probe gently at the base of the skull and deeply rather than at the center of the skull, this is her appearance.
Chapter Three.
On fractures that are not transverse.
If there is a fracture in the skull accompanied by pain and swelling that extends to the eye, the patient should be given medications for the head and all treatments mentioned in the illnesses section, if this does not help then the fracture remains in two places. The fracture can be treated with a sharp medicine or iron.
If the fracture is treated with a burning medicine, take a clove and grind it on both sides until it becomes powder. Then make an opening in the swollen area with a broad needle until it fits under the skin that can accommodate the powder.
He should enter it beneath the skin until it disappears, then press firmly on it with a broad instrument and leave it for ten hours, then dissolve it and extract the garlic and leave the wound for two or three days, then carry it.
He should anoint a boil with oil until the place softens, then treat it with the cautery, provided Allah wills, and if you wish, you can do this with some of the burning medicines mentioned in the thirteenth chapter among the burning medicines.
As for cauterizing with iron, it should be done with this characteristic: The container depicted in its image is to be heated.
The container with screws is called "Makwa al-Musmariyyah" because its top resembles a screw and has some slots in it, and there is a small hole in the middle of it.
Then put it on the location of the wound and hold it with your hand, while you slightly rotate the hot iron a little at a time, and the amount of burn from the skin should be similar to half of it. Lift your hand so as not to burn the nerves that are beneath it, lest there be leakage, then boil the boil in salt water and put it on the location for three days. Then the wound is smeared with oil, then it is treated with honey until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, seal this wound with a piece of skunk skin from the box and preserve it from festering in this wound specifically.
The Fourth Chapter.
Treatment of Fistulated Wounds.
If the wound is treated as we have mentioned in the treatment of various diseases and it does not heal, and you observe symptoms that are not described in our list of symptoms for the first category (disease with drugs or fire), then repeat the first treatment with either the drug or the fire. It is necessary to smear the skunk box until it turns white after you have marked its position on the wound with a line of approximately half a finger width or thereabouts and leave it for a moment before you press down hard enough to cut through the flesh and reach the bone.
It is necessary that you should preserve the connection of the jaw, for if it is burned, the nerve or muscle connected to it will be affected and result in numbness.
Be cautious and vigilant to avoid the spillage of blood from the severed flesh, for there is danger in it. Whoever is ignorant of what he does, and was not an experienced craftsman before, should leave the work to someone else.
This is the method of treating lateral nasal discharge from sinuses in its place, as written in the book, if Allah wills. If you find something incorrect with this technique, do not use it.
If you find the body of the patient suspected, make an incision in the middle of the head as we have described and treat the wound until it heals, if Allah wills.
If you want to use the method we mentioned in the chapter on treating sinuses with a probe equipped with two needles, it is better than this one and more effective.
Fifth section.
Treatment of ear injuries.
If there is an injury in the ear due to cold and it is easy to swell up, and all the treatments we have mentioned in the classification do not work, then insert the probe that is called "al-Nuqta" whose image is shown below.
Then, touch it with the probe around the entire ear as it rotates or around both of them together if the injury is in either one. Move the probe a little away from the center of the ear after determining its location by measurement. The probe should be about ten points in each ear or near that, then treat the locations until they heal, if Allah wills.
Sixth Chapter.
On Bloodletting.
The bloodletting, which is performed on the type of ailments that occur from phlegm, as described in the classification of diseases.
Avoid bloodletting on the type that occurs from congestion and paralysis of nerves.
When this type of bloodletting is done by venesection, cupping and leeching, and it does not yield a cure, then the cause should be sought out with three possibilities. One possibility is at the root of the ear, the second one slightly below the eustachian tube and the third one in the convergence of the eyes.
Make the incision on the side of the affected part, as the swelling only occurs in the visible area.
The bloodletting should be done with a long incision, opposite the upper ear, slightly below the hairline, and another one in the eustachian tube, of a length equal to the diameter of a pulse vein.
Lower your hand with the bloodletting instrument until it sears half a finger's thickness, and this is the shape of the cupping glass and it is a type of cupping known as wet cupping, which differs only slightly from the dry one as you can see. The scalpel should be of moderate sharpness, then treat the location as described until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Seven.
Bandaging the Lacerated Wound.
If bandaging and treatment as described does not heal, and it is not due to a hamstring injury, then lance the wound four times. On each quarter of the head, make a lance-wound as described and another in the middle of the head, and one on the convex part of the head according to what was mentioned.
The dressing method, as described, can also include a lance-wound on the nose of the ulcer, to make it deeper, then treat accordingly.
Chapter Eight.
Treatment for Nasal Fractures.
The cause of the fracture should first be irrigated with large syringes and healing ointments for the nose.
Then, the entire head should be shaved and a dressing made of kohl, as described in the article on bruises, applied to the affected area for several days, since it is a lancing tool.
Perform the same procedure on the location indicated earlier, if it heals with that, then lance three times in the convex part of the head from top to bottom of the neck.
Place a ligature between each incision finger, then treat the wound as presented. If you desire to increase (the number of fingers), and it is likely for that reason, tie the middle finger.
If you desire to increase (the number of fingers), tie the ends and treat it until it heals, and the knots are orange-like on the presented image.
The Ninth Chapter.
In the case of a hernia and the entire body swells up.
It is necessary to begin with cleansing the head using ear syringes and what we have mentioned earlier, then cut off the head of the affected area, make an incision in the middle of the head and one on each side of the head and another at the base (of the neck).
If the hernia causes the entire body to swell up and it is suspected that it might be more than that, and the patient is likely to have a strong and definite disease, tie four knots on the neck veins. The ligature should reach beyond the skin, lift your hand and treat it as mentioned before until it heals, God willing, and the knots are orange-like.
The Tenth Chapter.
In case of compound fracture.
If it is a compound fracture due to trauma, it should first be cleaned with large syringes and all the treatment mentioned in the section on wounds if the cause is severe and there is a possibility of administering medication.
If the patient is a child who cannot take medication, do not use forceps and instruments for cleaning the skull before that for several days with improvement of diet.
Then shave his head, then make a single incision in the center of the skull according to what is found in the characteristics and another incision at a later time. On each part of his skull, make an incision if the patient is strong and there is a possibility of it; then make the incisions mentioned in the "Falaj" owner and bind the body with belts at neck and waist areas, and let the wound be treated with oil according to its characteristics.
If the cause is a child, make the bandage gentle on this shape.
The tenth chapter.
In case of prolapsed anus.
If the cause of prolapsed anus is excessive and hard fecal matter, make the incisions mentioned in the "Falaj" owner.
If the cause of malnutrition is a distance from healthy food and the body of the patient is moist, wash it with that which cleans his brain, according to what comes forward in the process of dissection.
Then cut off the head of the patient, then make a firm cookie from walnut like in shape, then place it on the center of his head and the patient is sitting up, holding it from all sides. Then take one roasted lamb fat.
Then heat it on fire moderately until it becomes hot enough that a finger can be inserted into it, then empty it in the center of his head in the circle and leave it until it cools down. Perform this procedure every week along with all his good treatments until he recovers, if God wills.
If you wish to make small incisions on him, many of them but do not hold the scalpel in your hand, let it be an evaporation, for this type of incision will moisten the brain moderately.
Then place a damp cloth on him soaked in oil or chicken fat.
The second chapter.
In the case of water leakage in the eye.
If it is evident to you that the water leakage in the eye appears with the signs mentioned in dissection, then wash the patient's head and face from all moisture, clean his wound in the steam of the bath for several days.
Then make an incision at the top of his head and open a cavity in the center of the skull, then make two incisions on the temples if the flow of water begins in both eyes or from one side if it is in one eye.
Then cut with the saw all arteries and veins that are under the skin so that the cavities are in length as wide as the temples and preserve from bleeding.
If you see anything from it, cut it in its place with any treatment possible and the wisdom will come to you regarding the arteries and veins cutting and preserving from bleeding.
And there are two cavities under the cheekbones.
The third chapter.
In the case of collected tears.
If the tears of the eyes are collected continuously and have been before the arteries and veins that are on the surface of the head are cut off, and you suspect that this is due to a thick cold pus, then open the cavity which you described in the beginning of the flowing water. A cavity in the center of the skull, two cavities on the temples and two cavities under the cheekbones, and if more is needed, open a cavity on each side of the eyebrow with a small saw.
Chapter Fourteen.
In what way is the nostril to be cauterized.
If treatment as mentioned in the division does not improve, then apply cautery three nights later. Then cut off its head and remove the middle key with a cork made of olive oil. Then remove with a screw cork two keys above the eyebrows under the hair slightly, and keep the skin surrounding them intact, without cutting it. This is the image of the screw cork.
Chapter Fifteen.
In what way is the eyelid to be repaired.
If the eyelid is injured due to a disease or wetness, then remove one key from the eyelid with this crescent-shaped spoon.
If desired, remove two keys slightly above the eyebrows on both sides and keep a distance from the eyebrow and each key should be as long as the eyebrow.
Do not press the key too hard, only as much as a third of the skin can be burned and the shape of the spoon should be as shown here.
Chapter Sixteen.
In case of injury to the eyeball.
If the canthi are turned inwards, the eyeball will protrude. In this case, there are two methods to treat it. Either the method of burning (the protruding tissue) with fire, or the method of using a burning medicine, as for the former, the patient should be instructed to leave his canthi untouched until they grow back and align.
If the protrusion occurs when the canthi are growing, press on the eyeball with a blunt instrument so that it does not move until they grow back and align. When they have grown and aligned, place the patient's head on a stone and teach him to apply pressure on the eyeball using a piece of paper as a guide.
The guide should initially be placed close to the canthi, then a wet cotton swab is placed under the eyeball (either soaked in white of egg or blue dye). The swab-covered mold is then sealed with clay.
Then, the guide is slowly hardened in multiple stages until it completely burns the skin layer that resembles the paper ashes, clearly showing the result of your work as the eyeball is covered and the hair rises above the eyelid.
Lift your hand when the time comes, then leave it for three days, then wrap it in lard until the dry scabs disappear. Then treat it with mercury until it heals, if Allah wills. If hair reappears after a while and the wound is closed, apply cold cupping.
Prepare the area as before, if there is hair in the lower eyelid, pluck it until it returns to its natural position and no new hair grows from the eyelash. As for cauterizing with burning medicine, instruct the patient to leave the wounds open until they grow and level out.
Then make a figure out of the leather and cut it into an eye shape. Take from the holy soap and unboiled lye, one or approximately a dirham each, grind them together firmly using a mortar and pesticle, so as not to let it harden. Then spread it on the eyelid that you made into an eye shape and place it on one or two eyes, then put a soaked cotton under the eye and have the patient hold his head with your stone.
Put your finger on the medicine and press it slightly, while you move it when the patient feels the heat of the medicine as it is like fire. If the heat persists, leave the medicine and move it with your finger. When the heat subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
If you see the eyelid raised as it is during cauterization or cutting, otherwise treat with medicine at the place where the medicine has no effect and has not darkened until your work is completed and the eye burns. Then put cotton soaked in oil on it until the burning sensation subsides.
Then treat it with castor oil or something similar until it heals, and it is important during the treatment to ensure that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye. If the eyelid swells after days or if there is anything in the eye hair, remove it.
Make medicine specifically for that spot where the eyelid swelled, as you did first, then treat it until it heals. This is a picture of a horse's leaf.
Know that human eyes differ in size and depth, so adjust your cauterization technique accordingly. The correct method for healing is not hidden for those who have the skill in this craft.
Chapter Seven.
On a Nasr with an ulcer in the eye socket.
If treating the Nasr as described in the Treatises on Diseases does not heal, it is necessary to cauterize with this characteristic.
The al-Zahrawi commands that you place his head in your stone and hold his head between your hands, the servant, so that he does not move or shake his head.
Then put a swollen bandage in the white egg or in the eyepatch for his eyes, then cover the bowl that has this image on it.
Let it be in the form of a funnel like the nose of an eagle from one side that has the cavity, and if you wish it to be open on the other side, or if you wish it to be closed like a muzzle, except that this form is best for your work, if God wills.
Then you should squeeze the nose (of the animal) if it is open and draw out the gallbladder and blow it, or if it is not open then you open it and draw out the bile, then place the bowl over it, which is a very tight fitting bowl, and hold onto it with your hand until you reach the bone.
Keep your hand slightly away from the cavity towards the eye and towards the nostril, so as not to make a mistake or disturb the patient, for the bowl may fall into the eye and destroy it; if you have reached the bone in the first hole then do not repeat, otherwise prepare another bowl if necessary.
Leave it for three days, then apply a poultice of oil on it and treat it with dry mash (murr) until it opens up. If after forty days it has not opened up, apply the sharp purgative drug that dissolves bone to make it reveal the bone as will be explained in its respective chapter, if God wills.
The last face of the Nasir is mentioned among some of the noses, he goes to the place of the nose, then he chisels it, and places it inside the chisel in this form (image).
Pour a measure of lead, weighing a dirham, into it (the cavity) and hold the chisel firmly with your hand, well greased and without moving the small bone (the little finger) to avoid the lead getting into its eye. It is advisable to apply a poultice made of white egg or water on the eye of the small bone.
If the lead burns the nose and opens it in a strange way, then the nose will open according to what we have mentioned of the procedure and treatment, otherwise, there is no choice but to make an incision in the throat and guide the nose into the nasal passage in its appropriate place.
Chapter Ten.
In what kind of incisions for the eye.
In many cases of incisions in the eye, it is called 'shi'ra', and it happens especially in children's eyes. If this kind of incision is treated as we have mentioned in the section on treatment, the treatment does not work. Therefore, open a small, sharp-edged cup at this location.
Place the base of the cup on the edge of the knife and then place it in the incision until the cup reaches the depth of the incision. Then treat it with kiryot (a medical solution) until it heals, if God wills.
The Tenth Chapter.
In the case of nasal fracture in the mouth.
If a nasal fracture occurs in the althea, the gum or the roots of the teeth and swells then breaks and starts bleeding, and if it flows with pus, it becomes a nasal fracture. If this is treated and does not heal, it is necessary to apply a small cup over the nasal fracture.
Then insert a cup in the nasal fracture and hold it with your hand until the iron band covering it reaches its front and back and do this repeatedly. Then treat it as we have mentioned earlier, until it heals, if God wills.
If a member is severed and the flesh is torn away, otherwise it is necessary to examine its location and remove the rotten bone according to what will come out from it, if Allah wills.
Chapter Ten.
On fractures and dislocations that are difficult to reduce.
If the dislocation occurs due to moisture and the bones move and it is treated with medications without success, then place the head of the plaster in the socket, then pour the mortar that will come to resemble its shape after placing the tube on the tooth socket.
Place the plaster with a wooden handle in it and hold it slightly until the patient feels the heat of fire reaching the socket, then lift your hand, then return the plaster several times as you wish, then the mortar will fill up with brine water.
Hold it for an hour and apply it, then the moving bone will be fixed and the dislocated bone will harden and the rotten moisture will dry up.
Chapter One and Ten.
On toothache.
If the toothache is due to cold or there is pus in it and treatment with medications does not work, then apply heat on both sides of it, either by using heated oil or by applying fire.
If it is about the cupping with lard, it is that you take the beef lard, soften it in an iron pot or a copper pan, then take cotton and grind it on the edge of a vessel, then dip it in the softened lard and place it on the painful area with a roller and hold it until it cools.
Then repeat it several times until the heat of fire reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, dip cotton or wool in cold lard and place it on the painful area and put the heated iron over it until the heat of fire reaches the cavity of the tooth.
And if it is about cupping with fire, it is that you go to a copper or iron pipe and there should be some asbestos inside it so that the heat of fire does not reach the mouth of the person affected, then heat the vessel which has that shape and place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the vessel cools, do this several times.
Therefore, the pain may go away either on that same day or after another day, and it is advisable in case of cupping to fill the mouth of the affected person with good lard and keep it for an hour before bleeding, and this is the shape of the vessel.
"Describe in any direction and according to the ability, and this is the image of the intestine.
"The second chapter and the forty.
"Regarding camel bones.
"If the camel bones are from a fresh, cold and not spoiled animal and you want to set it quickly, then you heat the hollow vessel which is shown in the figure with both openings.
"To make the gas escape from the other side and place it covered on the same worm twice if necessary until you reach the depth of the worm, if the worm is small, then heat the vessel according to the size of the worm.
"Then leave it for three days, apply a cotton soaked in oil on it until what was burned disappears, then treat it with warm poultices and ointments until it heals, God willing.
"The third chapter and the tenth.
"Regarding camel humps with disorders of sound and shortness of breath.
"If coldness and humidity has affected the head of the camel hump, and there is no doubt that this is accompanied by a feverish state, it is necessary to empty the affected area first with easy medicines, then apply heat from the meat of the slaughtered animal at the base of the hump in the lower position.
Warning: Do not let the needle reach the bone, and do not burn the skin except half of it, then take another needle at the end of the incision in a long stitch, with the thread being a bandage on the side that advances.
Then treat it as described until he recovers, God willing.
The Fourth Chapter: Forty.
In the case of headache and toothache.
If the toothache and headache are due to cold moistness, without fever or inflammation, and if the disease is persistent: take two needles and insert one above each tooth in shallow and smooth hollows, and place another needle in the center of the chest between the breasts.
The thread should be a bandage, as shown in the figure that has been provided, and if desired, it can be a needle for puncturing with the needle known as the point, whose image has been shown in ear-puncturing. The points should be thirty or so.
Then treat it as described until he recovers, and a thread with three strands can be made on this figure to speed up the healing of the needle by using it in one three-needle treatment. This is the image of the bandage.
Chapter Fifty and Tenth.
On the topic of cataracts.
If the head of a bone (likely referring to the skull) protrudes due to swollen or unattached fluids, and it is not possible to set it during the initial attempt to reset it, then it should be allowed to occur regularly before attempting to reset it again. This should be done when the body part is subjected to the least movement, as we have observed in such cases. It is necessary that the jaw (fekk) be moved first. Then the artery (al-'aliil) is exposed either on the back or on the correct side, and then the skin that is inside the sheath (al-abts) is raised with your left fingers if the separation (al-mufsul) is intact. If it is split, it opens up within.
Then the bladder with the two colored spots (makwahat al-suffudin) is cauterized.
Then the skin is incised with it (the instrument) until it reaches the other side, and it takes a shape of four kiyas, and it may be cauterized with a bladder containing three sifawids, in which case the shape will be six kiyas, and the sifawids will be on the tip of the instrument.
This is an image of a bladder with three sifawids.
And this number (of kiyas) may be increased by one, making them eight, then salted grains and vinegar are placed on the kis, and the artery is tied off and no movement should be allowed for a while until it heals, whether the separation is above or not.
Put a single stitch or several tight ones above the navel, for the separation will widen and the moisture will drain and the artery will close off.
Chapter Six and Forty.
On Amputation.
If in amputation, coldness and excessive exudations occur to such an extent that they are expelled from their sockets and numerous pus discharges happen, and the patient is treated with various medications but fails to recover, it is necessary to draw the cause on his back, make an incision and cut off the limb, then bind it in three bandages. A bandage should be placed beneath the shoulder blade area, with a width of a finger in a buckle-like strap, and two bandages below the side of the single bandage until the bandages take the shape of a triangle and are separated from each other so that they do not meet, and the depth of the bandages should be approximately one-third the thickness of the skin, and the shape of the bandages should be triangular.
On this image and on this scale, nothing more.
If you wish, bind it with a large bandage in the center of the amputation on this image.
The buckle for this single bandage should be in the shape of a circle on this image.
The amputation is made to relieve the pain of those who are tortured by this limb, and it is taught on the amputation according to the desired measurement, then bound with a point-shaped buckle, and treated with the medication that is provided until the wound heals.
Chapter Seven and Forty.
On Cold Abdomen.
If there is exposure of the abdomen, ulceration from putridity or wetness, or foul smell to such an extent that its natural composition is disrupted with a discharge that is excessive and softening, without improvement as described in the classification, then it will not be beneficial (the treatment). The responsible person should lie on his back and learn by pressing three times in this way and to this extent on the abdomen, below the navel, where the human appendix ends.
After each press, let your fist be firm and the stroke along the body be straight, without bending your hand.
The pressure should be as deep as half the thickness of the skin, not more, and the person responsible should stand with both feet, if he cannot stand then he can sit supported by a staff and raise his arms. This is the image of the fist.
You can perform these pressures with a metal fist if you have an assistant and craftsmanship, and ensure that the pressure does not harm the skin so that it burns all the skin, burns the abdomen, reaches the intestines because the skin there is thin, so be aware.
The eighth and forty-first chapter.
In the abscess and tumor of the liver by incision.
If a swelling appears in the liver and you want to learn whether that tumor is in the liver tissue or its capsule, if it is in the liver tissue then it causes heaviness and pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the liver capsule, accompanied by severe sharp pain, you suspect that doctors have cured it, then it is necessary to locate the cause on its surface, then learn the location of the tumor by palpation.
Then, heat the pouch in fire, this is the pouch that resembles a mill and this is its image. Then, tie it with a single thread until the skin is completely burned and the tumor reaches the capsule so that all of the matter comes out, then treat it like an abscess until it is healed.
This type of tumor should not be used except by one who has long experience in medicine and has encountered these diseases many times, so when he encounters something similar to this work, he should proceed with it and leave it for someone better.
The ninth and forty-first chapter.
In case of dislocation.
Describing the initial steps of reducing a cold dislocation according to Zahrawan's principles, it is to take a long, slender bone splint from a dry yew rod as thick as a finger. Then it should be dipped in oil and heated in fire. Then, a single splint is made between the point of the shoulder and the neck, two small ones without needles near the side under the skin, and two large ones above the humerus bones between the third and fourth dislocations.
Two more splints are also between the fifth and sixth dislocations slightly behind, another in the middle of the chest, one above the clavicle, and three more from behind, one between the arms, and two below the arm splint that is located between the elbows.
Do not let your hand penetrate the splint, it should be on the surface of the skin with a thin coating. Some have reported that some people used a long iron spoon to protect it and insert it between the dislocations until it reaches the same place as the wound.
The abscess comes out as we have mentioned in the abdomen, and in this case it is filled with pus. Either the patient dies from his time or he remains exposed without any healing.
Chapter Thirty.
In the case of piles.
If you treat the disease of piles with what we have mentioned as treatment in the division, and it did not help, then on three aspects, all are correct: one is to tie them with three or four ligatures along the length of the piles.
In the shape of abdominal ligatures, which have the shape we have described for abdominal ligatures, and between each ligature there is a space sufficient for the length of a finger or more, and the knot of the ligature should be the same as the one we have described for abdominal ligatures and do not press hard with your hand on the ligature and the patient's position should be laid flat on his back.
The third aspect is by the ligature and raising the skin that is subject to the piles, where the ligature of the patient ends and raising the skin that is subject to the left piles and your lifting the skin should be on an extension of the body so that the ligatures are aligned along the length of the body.
Then the leeches enter a strongly protected place until they perform skin incision from the opposite side, then the cup is extracted making the cups four, and if you wish to cup with the three-toed leech's cup.
Treat the affected place after leaving it to be swollen for several days, it will be cured from all other treatments.
The First and Thirtieth Chapter.
On the cupping method.
The cupping only benefits in the method of bloodletting specifically, if you treat the one being bled with any other treatment mentioned earlier, your treatment will not be effective; it is necessary to cup four times around the affected area and once on the vein.
Another cup on the abdomen, one on the kidneys, two behind his back between the ribs, and one on the chest and another on the vein, the depth of the cup should be near to the skin puncture; then leave the cup open for a long time for swelling.
Do not leave the ill one from treatment after cupping, collect the meanings quickly by using it; the image of the cup used for the back will be ring-shaped as shown in its image, and the cup used for the chest will be cone-shaped.
Chapter Two Thirty.
On the Feet and Hands.
If a pain occurs in the joints and it is filled with white water, it should be bled on the back of the foot between the ankle and heel.
Place your hand on the lancet and do not bend it, then lift your hand and do not lower it again because it will cause the white water to flow out and the lancet will remain in this position.
Then bleed the hands twice in each hand, with the tip of the lancet from the side of the thumb on the lancet and the other at the length of the hand, one under the wrist and another below it towards the middle of the hand, and on each arm twice.
Leave the lancet open without any treatment for a long time so that water flows out from it, then treat it with all that has been mentioned before.
Chapter Three Thirty.
On the Rupture.
If the rupture is due to cold and swelling that weakens the mask and the pressure inside the abscess and it is suspected that it may be the cause of the rupture and its power has decreased, then make a large lancet on its cavity. According to what comes in any limb with a circular incision and four holes around the pit, sew gently with a fine thread, and a large knot or two on the skin above the tendon.
If you see pus and swelling likely, tie a knot on the abscess and one on each sideboob (translator's note: "khaisirah" refers to the armpit region in Arabic, and due to its proximity to the breast it could be mistakenly translated as "sideboob". However, for the sake of preserving the original text, I have kept it as it is.) and perhaps add two small knots on the limb close to the large one. This treatment is effective; may Allah grant benefit by it.
The Fourth and Thirtieth Chapter.
In the case of a seated patient.
If a seated patient has multiple or single veins that are hard and cold, or swollen pus-filled boils as we have described in the section on incision, treatment will not be effective. In this case, tie three knots below the navel slightly on the abdomen.
If the patient has a knot under the armpit like a thumb and if his limb is cold, he does not digest food, and his face appears swollen, tie a large knot on the limb where it comes out, and another one on the abdomen. Another one on a patient with an abscess, treat it with a ligation and leave the cavity open for some time, then heal it if Allah wills.
The Fifth Thirtieth Chapter.
On the topic of boils.
After cutting it, if the boil has been cut off, lance the cavity which resembles a mill, then place a drain in the same boil that was cut and hold your hand until the cavity reaches the opening of the anus from where blood will flow out. Do this once or twice.
If there are many boils, treat each one as we have described and heal it with the appropriate ointment until healed. And if the cavity is large on the skin, it will be more beneficial.
The Sixth Thirtieth Chapter.
On the topic of the Nasal Ulcer which occurs in the nasal cavity and its surrounding areas.
If no cause is present for the ulcer and the treatment we have described in its place does not work, it may not heal by itself. If a nasal ulcer occurs and pus and harmful exudates run from it, first you should narrow it with a thin string.
Then, recognise the bladder by the string, then fill the bag that resembles a bladder, and insert it into the same location of the bladder with precision, keeping in mind both the position of the bladder and the place where the string has entered. Then prepare the cauterisation tool until those corrupt tissues are burned, either once or twice or thrice according to your need.
And beware of burning the nerve if there is one present, or a large vein, and if the bladder is leaking pus or urine.
Keep away from these places, and do this only if the bladder is in a healthy condition and you are certain it is not perforated. Then treat the place until it heals, if it is stitched and the materials removed, and it remains like that for some time, then know that it has been completely healed.
If the materials are not removed, then know that it is perforated or in a bladder abscess or something similar as mentioned in its location.
The seventh and thirty-seventh section.
In the kidney cauterisation tool.
If there is pain in the kidney, or fever and thick breath with a decline in health, all causative factors should be eliminated. Then bind it on the affected side of the same kidney using a bandage made of twisted threads as mentioned earlier, and perhaps three bandages in the same belly cavity. This will lead to three tightly bound bandages which will be more effective.
Chapter Eighty-third.
On the incision of the bladder.
If weakness and urging to urinate occurs in the bladder due to cold or moisture that prevents the obstruction of urine, the physician should perform an incision in the lower part of the abdomen on the bladder where the hair of the navel begins, and one incision from the right side of the abdomen and another from the left.
And after the incision, from each side should be tied a ligature and an incision made in the lower abdomen or two if necessary, and the wound should be sutured with a suture that follows the edge of the cut.
Chapter Ninth-thirty.
On the incision of the womb.
If there is matter from cold or moisture in the womb, one should abstain from coitus and suturing her wound is difficult or if it ruptures during childbirth or causes pain, then three incisions should be made around the abdomen as we mentioned in the incision of the bladder. An incision on the abdominal pouch below the navel or two incisions, and the wound should be sutured with a suture.
Chapter Forty.
If a dislocation of the shoulder occurs.
If a dislocation of the shoulder occurs, it is possible that incorrect moisture reaches the joint causing it to dislocate. Its sign is that one side becomes longer than the other if they touch each other and you find a gap where the dislocation has occurred. In this case, it is necessary to return the cause to the joint itself using a circular motion.
After learning about the method of setting a bone in the same way that it rotates to be in the center of the circle, and if the tool used for setting does not have this shape, then use three tools similar to the large olive-shaped setter.
Sharpen the instrument deeply, up to the point of piercing the skin completely, then apply it until the patient screams, if God wills it.
The forty-first section.
If a female's private part is torn apart.
If a fracture occurs in the joint and the cause of it was cold and moisture, and treatment has been applied according to what we have mentioned in the sections, but the treatment did not succeed and the time for that has elapsed, then it is necessary to remove the hard clots with warm oil or warm water and similar things.
Then apply the cautery to the cyst and make a small incision in it with either hot cautery or fire. When using fire, there will be many cysts on various faces; one of them should be cauterized precisely at its base with three points similar to a triangle as shown in this image.
It should be cut deeply, and between each point there should be a space equal to the width of a fingernail. The cyst should be oily and there should be a single cautery at the center of the cyst itself so that there are four points altogether. If desired, it can also be made in the shape of a circle as described earlier when removing the cyst.
The circle should encompass the entire cyst and burn off all the surrounding skin; this is the property of the cautery for a woman if the wound is due to the cyst itself and does not extend to the limbs or genitals.
If it extends to the limbs or genitals, apply two cauteries at the location indicated by the cause of the wound in that area and a cautery above the anus with four fingers towards the hairy side; the cyst should be lancet-shaped, and the depth of the cautery should only reach as deep as burning the skin.
If it appears that the wound extends towards the fingertips of the leg, make an incision where you indicate with three or four or more stitches if necessary. If it indicates the wound is beneath the saddlebone towards the tailbone, make an incision there, but only a single sharp knife incision.
Keep in mind, in all cases, do not let the knife reach nerves or large blood vessels as this can cause severe pain or delay healing.
You have witnessed two individuals, one with a wound on the top of the head and another in the knee where the knife has reached all the way to the ankle and crushed it, damaging the entire leg, then there was swelling and death occurred later. Therefore, if the wound is on both sides like this, be aware of it.

After each false boil, there should be a distance equal to the thickness of a hair, and the false boils should be open from both sides and their height should be like a coin or two coins. Take a lock for them made of iron that has been tempered well in the false boils, this is its shape.
Then, it is heated in the fire until it turns red and the pus is drained. Then, it is placed on the correct position and left at rest on the healthy side. It is then punctured three times in one place, then left for three days, softened with oil, and the wound is kept open for days.
Many (boils) then are treated with lard until it bursts, as stated in this book; we have used this type of ink for our craft and its appearance is pleasing, and only a few can endure it who are skilled at using it, it being good for those who can endure it and receive treatment.
As for the boil treated with burning medications, it is to make cups resembling needles into which a lead or iron ball falls.
In their cavities, there should be a height of two or more fingers and below that the width of a fingertip. They should both be open from bottom to top and bound together in this shape.
Then, they are placed on the correct position and left at rest on the healthy side with the hand pressed firmly. Next, water is poured between the two circles which is heated slightly and held for an hour. The patient bears it and it burns the boil. For it finds the boil like fire.

Apply the leech until the wound is healed. If the wound extends to the foot or ankle, make a watertight container according to the size of the cautery and fill it with the same water. This is the property of the hot water, which has been proven in the article on remedies.

Galenus claimed a story of a man from the Qadma people as a treatment for scourge and vaginal pain, and emphasized his command greatly, claiming that he does not need any other treatment and that it cleanses once.

It softens and leaves for three hours or until the pain ceases to be severe before immersing it in the hot bath. If pus is released from his body, immerse him in the tub. The wound will heal with God's permission; if it does not heal, repeat the treatment after ten days.

The knife shall be sharp, take wool and soak it in old oil to be applied to the deep spot between the finger joint and the wrist, nearest to the wrist. Then take a dry male mule anus.
Heat it in fire until it becomes a small ball, then place it on the wool and leave it until it cools down, then take another one and continue this process until the pain reaches the middle of the arm and the wound settles with God's permission. This treatment is known as the mule's anus strike.
The second and forty-fourth section.
In case of abdominal pain.
In case of abdominal pain, it may be due to various reasons such as falls or blows or ruptures and similar. It may be caused by the impact of cold and wet material, and this type is specific to itself.
The one caused by the impact of cold material should be treated after evacuating the cause, i.e., by applying heat to the abdomen where the pain is, in three layers corresponding to the width of the abdomen itself, after locating the position with a probe in each layer, with five or more dots according to the possibility and strength of the cause.
The one caused by puncture wound should be treated with needle-punctures, and if you prefer, it may be punctured three or four times with a medium-sized suturing needle on this figure.
The third and fourth chapters.
In case of starting boils.
This disease often occurs in small children, and a sign of its onset in the child is that he experiences shortness of breath during activity and movement, and you will find, in the end, pus-filled boils that may extend over other boils.
If you see that and wish to immobilize it, then tie it with a round ligature as shown in this figure. Take a ligature on all sides of the branch, and if you wish to tie it around the branch with a single or triple knot, make sure the knots are close together, then treat the area until it heals as we have described.
Keep in mind that the ligature is to be used for a nerve that has been severed.
Chapter Four and Forty.
On ligatures for fractures and dislocations.
If the dislocations are due to cold swellings in any part of the body, when such injuries occur in both legs, they are commonly referred to as specific fractures.
If the specific fracture is due to treatment as described in the previous section and the injury does not go away, then tie it after the swelling has gone down with multiple ligatures around the dislocated knee joints, using moderate size needles in this manner.
If you need to ligate on the surface of a leg, use a single knot. If the injury rises to the knees or other joints and this often happens, tie it around each knee with three or four ligatures from all sides using this moderate size needle.
If the wound is larger than this, press it and do not dig your hand into the wound but only to the depth of skin thickness. If the wounds reach the armpit or the back, use what we have mentioned about the cataplasms in its chapter.
If the wounds are only in the hands, press around the fingers as one would turn a pair of tweezers. If the wounds remain on the fingertips or on the palm, press each spot individually and on the joints of the hand. If the wounds continue after several days to the joints or knuckles.
Press both from all sides and do not leave any space for the wound to heal improperly or take medicine as it is better to have good food and relieve gas, for this cataplasms will help if God wills with food.
The fifth and forty-fourth chapter.
On the cataplasms of burns.
If a burn appears in the armpit and some skin and fat is burned and this begins near, it is necessary for the patient to fast on that day and use from the malmis a substance which removes blisters from its depth.
Then he lies down between your hands on his back and orders him to hold himself until the fat or skin blisters appear, then you flatten it with a fingertip, then teach him to rub gently under the burn mark on the bone of pain which resembles half a circle with its edges towards the top of the body.
Then boil this pot of its shape.
Then wait for the egg white to coagulate, then pour or apply the medication/salve into its cavity. The attendant should place his hand on it so that it does not move, and having opened between the little fingers, place it under them and close with a bandage, and another attendant ties it up.
And lastly, hold the pot on the mark with one hand, then lower the pot onto the spot itself and your other hand on the pot, stand still and hold it until it reaches the bone or return it again if it does not reach the bone in the first attempt.
Keep your effort from moving the medication pot so that it does not burn the patient, for this may cause either death or great harm. Know that when you do not reach the bone with the tool, your work has not been successful. It is necessary that the pots for children be gentle according to their abilities, and for adults according to their abilities.
Then treat the wound with oil for three days until the scab of fire disappears, then treat it with other medications until it heals. The patient should remain lying on his back for forty days until the wound is closed.
It is recommended that food be a treatment duration for him, which does not irritate his abdomen when it passes, lest the pain reoccur and then, if he wishes to continue after forty days, use strict bindings and hold them for another four days, reducing fatigue and overloading from food, drink and fluids.
If he follows this method, his condition will be alleviated, insha'Allah. I shall now explain the treatment for a fistula in the anus, if Allah wills, and as for a fistula occurring elsewhere in the abdomen and starting intermittently, if you wish it not to worsen, make a simple fistula from it at his discretion. Let a third of the skin be burned and treat it as we have described, insha'Allah. Some early authorities have recommended that the fistula be stopped with a plug-like device resembling this image.
After you have learned about the fistula, draw a line on its upper side and another one below it. Then lower your hand to the center with one finger (or thumb), wrap the first finger (or thumb) loosely around the fistula, if Allah wills.
Sixth and Forty-Fourth Chapter.
On Various Wounds.
If a wound occurs in one of the limbs due to falling or hitting and the pain persists for a long time without healing with medication, it is necessary to cauterize with a puncture-type cautery and adjust it according to the size, smallness, weakness, and strength of each limb.
After the wound or injury is cauterized, if it does not heal, the cautery should be repeated because it is common for these types of wounds to move from one limb to another nearby. Therefore, the cautery must follow it until the cause is eliminated.
Seventh and Forty-Fourth Chapter.
On Fractures.
As for fractures, they can greatly benefit from cautery, whether it is a clean or unclean fracture. The type of fracture that occurs due to the softening of the bone and marrow should be cauterized.
If you wish to probe, observe first if the patient's condition is initial and if treated as described in the section of incision, and it neither closes nor stops, suspect that corruption may affect all its humors. Keep him on his head for five days. In the middle of the head, the first one is below it towards the nape at the end of the hair, the second is two on the horns and one from behind on the occipital bone, and press your hand gently with the probe until it affects the bone slightly easily.
Remove skin from him to ease the thick phlegm from it and press the probe on the same place as it advances, and if the tumor persists by suspicion and appears clearly, this set of keys mentioned in the head should be used. A key on the side of the nose, two on the cheeks, two on the temples, four on the shoulders, one large one at the elbow joint and another above it in the same arm, and two on each wrist. Two on the palms and one on each finger, and two on each foot, and one on each ankle, and a key for every joint of his hands and feet.
Preserve the nerve that is on the rear of the skull, lest you burn it. It may touch a bone in the ear, another in the mouth, and another in the abdomen. Know that every time you apply the cautery, it will be beneficial and safe.
The reason the cautery does not find its mark and the correct one does, is because the former has become hard due to aging, and it is essential that the wounds are large for the muscles and small at joints in accordance with the characteristics of the bones.
Then treat the wound with fine crushed cornsalves and other treatments until, may Allah have mercy, it heals.
Chapter Eighty Four.
In a hard wound, when a limb of one of the body's parts is affected and treated with medicines, ointments, and dressings but does not heal, it is necessary to cut off the same limb with cauterization on the bone or smaller in accordance with its size or smaller, so that the cautery may be deep in the skin a little.
Then treat it with honey until it heals, and for some hard wounds that expose the hand or leg in the chest area near the exit of the nerve that moves that limb, the wound will heal by itself.
Does not approach that except one who is skillful in the dissection of limbs and the excision of movable body cavities.
The ninth and forty-fourth chapter.
On scabies.
If scabies occurs and no remedy from the remedies of medicine works on it, then apply to it a small amount of depth so that the white disappears and its color changes.
Then it is treated with powdered cassia leaves mixed with oil of wormwood, camphor or castor oil from each part, all combined and applied to the skin until it heals. The position must be maintained until it heals.
The fifty-first chapter.
On cancer.
If cancer is at its beginning and you want to stop it, then apply a ring of lead around it as it rotates, and some scholars have said that one should apply a plaster in the middle of it, but I do not see that because I expect that it will rot and I have seen this several times.
The correct way is to apply a ring around it as we said, or with several plasters.
The hundred and fifty-first chapter.
On gout.
If a tooth becomes diseased in a patient, and it has become putrid either from the active agent causing it or from the predisposing cause, if the patient is elderly and has little blood, and you wish to hasten the extraction of the tooth, surround it with small sharp picks.
Then leave it, for it will hasten in extraction. If you wish to loosen it with a lever, prepare the mortise (mortar hole), as shown in this figure.
Pull it out in the middle of the tooth until the pulp is exposed, and place the lever below it to facilitate the extraction. Then treat it as necessary until it heals.
Chapter Two, Fifty-Six.
On the topic of leeches.
Leeches are a disease that affects the body, just as fire consumes dry wood. If you see leeches in a place where there may be a sore near a fire, prepare small and large iron mortises in accordance with what is appropriate for that location where the leech is found.
Then extract it from all sides until all the disease has been removed and there remains nothing of the leech, then leave it for three days and apply the mortar holes with powdered quicklime mixed with oil to cause the blisters and all the pus to burst.
Then treat it with a cautery for meat. If you find after three days that the meat is growing a plant properly, there is no harm in it. Otherwise, repeat the procedure on the corrupt areas, and the eater can be treated with the sharp drug.
It stands faster by fire for benefit, and I have mentioned its treatment with the sharp drug in the division section. Take it from there whenever necessary.
The third and fifty-fifth chapter.
On the subject of curved and non-curved iron needles.
This happens frequently in the soles of feet and it is something hard that a man may suffer from, and the needle is on it on two sides: either the hot needle or the sharp cold one.
As for the hot needle, it is to heat a long curved iron probe resembling an eagle's beak made of iron with a handle on both sides and sharp at the tip, then lower it onto the iron splinter from all sides and rotate your hand with the probe around the iron splinter until the probe reaches the depth of the iron splinter.
Leave it for three days to heal, then press it with a clean, sharp leech that has been salted, and leave the leech on it overnight. It will discharge from its roots, then treat the wound with fresh meat fat until it heals, provided the pins are not crossed.
It often occurs on the surface of the body, particularly on the hands and feet. A tube made of copper, iron or eagle feather should be taken and placed over the vein or artery. Then water should be poured into the tube with sufficient force to stop the bleeding.
Hold your hand firmly and press gently with your other hand to make the tube press hard against the vein, so that the water reaches the root of the vein. Allow the water to flow into the tube for a short time.
Then leave it, as the vein will discharge from its roots. Repeat this process until it has been removed from all parts of the body. Then treat the wound with fresh meat fat when it has discharged, and allow it to heal.
The Fourth and Fiftieth Section.
In case of fracture.
If any fracture happens in the bones of the arm or leg, it is required to tie four or five splints on the back between each splint and also one at the chest. And on his side, a splint with almond oil, for the fracture heals and speeds up the cold disease.
The fifth and sixth chapters.
In case of sudden internal swelling.
If sudden internal swelling occurs due to heavy, rotten, poisonous substances, it is necessary upon its appearance to tie a soft splint on each swelling and then heat the tip of the splint with fire or long ashes, or with eggshells.
The fractures occur initially in this state, and the active principle for them does not increase, but the cause of it abates except that it should be after the evacuation of the cause by cutting.
The sixth and fiftieth part.
In case of fracture when the arteries are cut.
Frequently, the fracture of a bone occurs from cutting of arteries due to injury, or breaking and wound, or any limb, etc., it becomes difficult to cut (them).
If any of these (conditions) happen to someone, hasten your hand to the place of the arteries and put your thumb on it and press firmly until the blood is confined under your thumb and nothing comes out of it, then put small and large clay pots filled with olive oil near it and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the arteries have been cut, and lower the tourniquet on the same arm after you have removed your finger with the forceps, and hold the tourniquet until the blood stops.
If the arteries are cut during your removal of a finger, and the tourniquet is released, take another tourniquet with forceps from those prepared in the fire, and continue to do so one after another until the blood stops.
And keep a knife handy in case there is no other means of treating the wound, and be aware that if the arteries release blood they will not stop it except by one of four methods: either by burning as we mentioned, or by cauterizing with a hot iron if the wound has not become putrefied. If it is putrefied and the blood is cut, or if it can be bound with strong and secure stitches, or if medicines are applied to it that have the ability to stop the bleeding and strengthen it strongly.
And as for the one who tries to stop it with ropes or by pressure, or placing heated objects near it and similar things, that wound will not be stopped except in the case of a minor injury; if anyone tries this method and no doctor or medicine is present, he should place the thumb on the wound as we described.
He must press it strongly until the blood is confined, and be cautious on top of the wound and on the arteries and veins; do not let cold strong water flow over it continuously, for fear that the blood may clot, harden, coagulate and cut off, during which time one should consider what it requires in terms of any or medicine.
The Second Chapter.
In incisions, wounds, fractures, surgeries and similar matters.
It has been said before in the first chapter that every illness can be cured with fire and burning medicine, its causes, instruments, and methods of application, as well as descriptions of cauterization tools. This is a summary from antiquity to modern times.
And in this chapter, I shall explain that path clearly for the benefit of the student.
Before I begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter deals with cauterization, which was mentioned in the first chapter on fire and burning medicine.
Therefore, it is important to take a more serious warning because the work in this chapter often involves a loss of blood which is essential for life when an artery or vein is opened or cut during an incision or wound, abscess drainage, surgical procedure, removal of a tumor or wounding on a bone or similar matters, all of which are accompanied by fear and anxiety and death occurs in many cases.
I advise you concerning the occurrence of ambiguity in your practice, indeed it may happen to you in this craft, people with quivers of needles among them, some of whom have been stricken by their disease and death approaches him.
The sharpness of his needles and the length of his incisions, and the impending illness that indicates death; among them is one who will spend for you from his wealth and benefit you with it in hope of health and the fight against his disease. Therefore, do not assist him whom you know to be of this treacherous character.
Be aware, your caution should be greater than your desire and be careful not to attempt anything of this nature without a certain knowledge that the outcome will be praiseworthy for you. Use in every treatment for your illnesses the advancement of knowledge and warning about what leads to safety.
In this matter, there is help for you in gaining praise, glory, remembrance and honor. May Allah guide you, and not deprive you of success, for that is within His power; none has the power except Him.
This chapter is long on what comes before the hand in the chapter of the foot, so that you may avoid the desire for what you seek from it if God wills.
Chapter One.
Treatment of water that accumulates in the heads of children.
This pustule frequently occurs on the heads of children during birth, if a susceptible mother presses the head of the child without support, it may also occur due to unknown causes.
I have not seen this cause in anyone other than children, and all whom I saw from them died quickly for this reason, so I saw leaving treatment of it and I have seen children whose heads were filled with water and the head swells daily. Until the child does not sit on himself to swell his head and moisture increases until it kills him.
This moisture either gathers between the skin and bone or it gathers under the bone on the scalp, and the treatment in this case is if the moisture is between the skin and bone and the abscess is small, it should be opened in the center of the head with a single incision about two fingers long to relieve the moisture, and this is the appearance of the lancing.
If the moisture increases and the abscess is larger, make two connected incisions in this shape:
If the moisture is beneath the bone, and it's indicated by the fact that you see open stitches from all sides and the water lowers when you squeeze it with your hand, do not hide this. You should make three incisions in the center of the skull at this point.
After making the incisions, all the moisture comes out, then close the incisions with sutures and ointment. Leave it uncovered for the fourth day, then dissolve the stitches and treat the wound with oil and honey, do not leave the skull open for too long, and feed the patient a little dry food, low in moisture.
Until the limb recovers and becomes well, another treatment for an abscess is to look for the place where the bone of the tumor appears and collect the water that has accumulated there, as it may be deeper in the skull or more towards the rear or on the right or left side.
By incision, find the place where the tumor appears and drain the water from there, then cut into the flesh as much as you can, causing a flow that will make the patient die from the seepage along with the release of moisture.
The Second Chapter.
Division of the two arteries situated behind the well-known ears, known as the temporal.
If a sharp edged lesion appears on the eyes or chest and treatment with medication fails, then treatment for this is amputation of these two arteries.

Then teach them to amputate both (limbs) at the joint, then cut them off at the elbow socket, divided into bones up to the skull's width. If you wish, enter the arm from below the armpits and turn it upward through cutting, with the length of the cut approximately two joined fingers.
If a finger is cut, blood will spurt out forcefully, flowing towards the face and wet clothes, unless the arteries are felt. In such case, one should measure from the ear three fingers' width, then teach amputation at the joint and cut to the bone. This should be done.
Blood will flow in streams or perhaps more or less, depending on the strength of the wound and feeling of the arteries. Then, one should look at the injury; if any part remains on the bone from the nail, it should be cut off.
