The Third Chapter.
On the amputation of the two fingers in the palms (of the hand).
If a man develops a persistent or sharp painful swelling in the palms of his hands or fingers, or if his finger is suddenly and severely crushed and he is unable to receive proper medical treatment for it, we have found effective treatment for such conditions through amputation of the affected limbs as described previously.
The goal of the procedure is to shave the hair that is in the armpit and the visible hair on the head, for it becomes clear to you from its bleeding and the scanty hair that is not apparent among people.
If it is cold, it is hidden from you. Therefore, shave the hair of his neck by virtue of his clothes, then massage or heat the site with hot water until the hair appears clearly and distinctly. Then take the lancet that has this image. Then cut the skin with it until you reach the hair, then place a lancet in it and draw it to the top until it comes out of the skin and remove it from the scabs that are under it from every side. If the hair is fine, tilt the lancet towards one side. Then cut a piece of it to the extent that its sides are separated, bleed and do not cause bleeding but if it does not burst and is not cut, it will not flow blood at all. Then empty the blood from it with six or three poultices.
If the hair is thick, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong thread. The thread may be from a linen cloth or from the strings of a bow, so that pus does not accumulate before the wound heals and bleeding occurs.
Then, make the incision between the sutures. Perform this at that hour or a later time, and if you wish to tie a ligature onto the bone with a fine needle until its edges grow together. This position for such an operation should be done with care or even better, as we have said.
After that, tie the ligature between the sutures. This is beneficial for preventing infection or inflammation of the wound, and it should be done after the skin is sutured. Then, the area should be bandaged with clean linen cloths, and ointment medication should be applied until healing occurs, God willing.
If, while performing your work, some blood leaks out, either cut it with a needle or fill the area with a dressing and press firmly until the bleeding stops. If no such thing occurs, place your finger over it to let the bleeding clot.
Submerge the area in cold water until the swelling subsides and press on it as necessary, and this is easier than suturing the wound with needles after learning the points of the incision.
The amputation should be performed by a skilled surgeon until it reaches the bone, and the artery should be cut in two places to allow for separation of the ends. This is not causing harm with this type of cauterization, and this is an illustration of an amputation.
The points of the cauterizing irons should resemble small needles but be less sharp, because if they were as sharp as needles, the cold would reach them faster and the flesh would not separate quickly. If there is any hesitation in their use, hold them over the fire.
The flesh is cut quickly, and this procedure is better than any other, less painful and easier. Let the space between the cauterizing irons be as wide as the width of a finger.
Chapter Four.
Treatment of chronic watery eye discharge.

Then make three incisions in the forehead, aligned along its length. The length of each incision should be approximately two finger-widths. Save the two severed vessels that are on either side and keep a distance from them. The gap between each incision should be approximately three fingers' width. Always have a prepared ligature or forceps with many fine needles to stop bleeding.
Then insert the pointed stylet, as shown in this image. From the upper incision towards the central incision, cut all the skin and fat between them using a scalpel on the bone. Repeat this process from the central incision to the lower incision, then remove the stylet. Enter the first incision with another tool called a scalpel, sharp on one side and blunt on the other. The Sixth Chapter.
Treatment of what falls into the ear.
Everything that falls into the ear can be one of four types: mineral such as stone or metal like iron and glass, or plant material like beans and grains, or liquids like water and honey, and other similar substances.
If an animal falls into the ear, a stone or something that does not belong in the ear, accept sunlight on it; if you see the stone, press oil (or wax) into it with a syringe or tweezers, then try to remove it by moving the head or vibrating with reeds. Close the ears of the patient when the pus or scabs have settled around the ear, and then tilt the head upwards; often it will be expelled by this treatment. If not, try to remove it gently with a plier, which is its shape as depicted here.
If it is removed with the plier and not, try to remove it with a thin copper funnel, its diameter being as small as possible; if this does not work either, make a tube of copper and insert one end of the tube into the ear canal.
Close the mouth of the tube with molten lead so that air does not find another way out than the tube, then draw it out with strong suction and often it will be expelled by this; if it does not come out as described above, take a feather or a thin stick that birds use to pick up small things and put it into one end of the tube.
After a boil has hardened on him, then insert it into the ear canal after the ear has dried from moisture, if it does not come out as we have described, then one should dig it before the hot swelling or inflammation occurs.
The method of digging is to press the boil in the ear canal first and make it bleed as much as its strength allows, then hold the boil between your fingers and tilt the head so that the ear is facing upward, and then dig a small hole at the bottom of the ear where it is tender.
The digging will be like a hollow sphere until it reaches the boil, then remove it with whatever tools you have, and quickly sew up the hole from where you dug, and treat it until it heals.
If the thing that fell into the ear is one of the seeds which grow and swell, try to remove it with what we have mentioned; if you cannot remove it, then grab a thin stick gently on this figure.
Try to cut that type of seeds which fell into the ear, and you only do this if you are certain that the seed has become moist with the steam of the ear until it becomes soft and in small pieces; then remove them with a pair of tweezers or a soft probe or a pincer.
As we have mentioned, it is easy to remove [the foreign body]. Regarding the water inside the ear, it should be treated first with olive oil or mustard oil, then plug the affected ear with some wool soaked in warm water. If the water comes out with this.
Take many small, smooth stones and warm them slightly in fire, then extract oil from one of them and insert it into the ear canal. Plug one end of a stick with this oil and strike the stone at the other end repeatedly until it breaks and falls out.
Continue this process with different stones until all the water is removed. Water can also be extracted by using a feather or reed, insert one end into the ear and heat the other end with fire until it burns more, then replace the reed with another one.
Continue this process until all the water is removed or draw out the creature within by using a syringe attached to the hole in the stone, and for removing small creatures such as a maggot, treat it as mentioned in the previous section.
If the body part is large enough to feel, attempt to extract it using forceps and curettes. It will be easier than treating anything in the ear. As for removing the pus that develops in the ear, if you have treated it as we described in the article on boils, but your treatment has not been successful.
It is necessary to observe the ear in sunlight, if something from pus appears, extract it with forceps or soft curettes. If nothing appears, take this tube-like object for examination.
Squeeze the lower part and widen the upper part, then gently insert a thin strip into the ear up to its limit. Then press firmly several times until all pus is expelled. If it does not come out, you should rotate the tube around with cotton as I have instructed in the chapter on earwax.
If it does not come out as described, use the ear drops that I have mentioned earlier in the treatment of pus and you will find them in the chapter on ear drops. Your salve and medication should be placed in the ear using this device, see its image here:.
As you can see, it is made of silver or copper, with a narrow bottom and a wide top. The plunger inside the tube should be made of hard copper, and if you wish, you can take a small rod and wrap it in cotton to press firmly.
Then, apply oil or ointment (or any desired medicine) into the ear tube (i.e., funnel), and let it be in the ear. Then enter the patient gently with your little finger and crush it (the medicine) with your fingers until fat is expelled into the depth of hearing and it becomes audible.
Then, place the hot material (that causes irritation in the ear) into a container and let it cool slightly to avoid causing discomfort or excessive heat to the ear, as the ear cannot withstand extreme cold or extreme heat.

Treatment for Perforation of Ear.
Some children may be born with an undeveloped ear canal, not pierced.
Moreover, perforation in the ear canal may also occur due to injury or accumulated pus within it, and this perforation can be deep inside the ear canal, not visible by the eye.
If the perforation is near the surface and visible, it may be easier to treat, but if it's deep within the ear canal and not visible, it can be difficult to cure, and in such cases, it is advisable to expose the affected ear to sunlight. If you see the perforation clearly, open it gently with a thin tool to give the following appearance: (Illustration of ear canal and perforated area).
The edge of it should be slightly narrow, limited in some parts and wider on the other sides, so as not to harm the ear. If the wound is over the muscle, it may grow into the auditory canal, in which case grasp it gently with a thin forceps and cut it vigorously until all the flesh is removed.
If the wound is in the depth of the ear, take a thin probe gently and soften it slightly in the fire, then insert it into the auditory canal. If you feel the probe with what accompanies it of hearing loss, break it vigorously.
Preserve the hearing of the ear and fill it with a salve in proportion to the size of the wound, as is done in the Egyptian method, do that for several days until you are assured of safety from infection or take the salve and apply it to water, then crush it into powder.
If you see the ear has become inflamed and a hot boil appears on it, it is necessary to remove the salve and replace it with another that is made from castor oil until the fever subsides, then treat it until it recovers.
If bleeding occurs, immerse cotton or linen in cold water and place it on the ear and apply all treatment for stopping the mentioned bleeding as described in the chapter on cauterization.

The tenth chapter.
Treatment of the sinusitis that occurs in the nose near the eye.
Sinusitis is a congestion occurring in the upper layers of the nose, which affects children more and weighs on their eyes. It causes migraines during the mornings and they are unable to see clearly in the sunlight. To make the tears flow towards it.
Therefore, they lie with their faces constantly against it and sleep on it, making their eyes water. If the inflammation does not appear in the initial incision, it is necessary to increase the incision slightly and then wait until the inflammation appears. Then pull it out as previously mentioned, then immerse the catgut in salt water and place it on the spot and press it firmly, some people use vinegar.
He should place it in the cavity of the abscess to drain any remaining moisture, then treat it until it heals. If it becomes inflamed in its position and a hot abscess occurs, treat it with cautery until it heals.

The second chapter.
On lifting the hair from the eye with an iron hook.
If the hairs involved in this are long, take a thin iron hook and insert a fine, soft thread into it, then tie its ends together with a very fine knot, making sure that the length of the thread is about the thickness of a grain.

The Third Chapter.
Treatment of the Shotra (cataract) that occurs in the upper eyelid.
This cataract, called Arnbiyyah, can be either natural or acquired. The acquired cataract is due to injury or trauma, or similar causes.
The treatment for this cataract is to break the injury, separate the eyes and place a cotton wool between them until it heals, without using anything that dries or shrinks.
If you do this, the cataract will return with greater intensity or you may use things that cause irritation such as onions, garlic, water with salt and vinegar, camel urine and the dung of donkeys which have been mixed with something from a dead animal and burned to heal it.
The healers of this cataract are those who treat it with all sorts of methods, but never touch the area where it was initially, and this procedure that we have mentioned is one method to correct the cataract, not to return the initial state of the eye.

Treatment of the hernia that is in the lower abdomen.

Chapter Thirty.
On Extraction of Teeth.
It is necessary to treat the tooth from its pain by every means, and it is possible not to extract it if there is no need for extraction since it is noble until it becomes necessary to extract it.
If the cause for extraction is firm, it is necessary that you confirm the tooth's pain so that the tooth becomes sound with you. Often, the cause for pain is deceived and it is thought that it is in a healthy tooth, so it is extracted, but the pain does not go away until the sick tooth is extracted; we have seen this many times from the actions of the dentists.
If the tooth's pain is clear with you, then it is necessary to tighten around the tooth with a grip in it with some strength until the pus is discharged from all sides, then move it with your fingers or soft tweezers gently back and forth until it loosens.
Then, when the larger dogs are enabled, we enable it well and place the patient's leg between them so that they may grip it firmly, rendering it motionless. Thereafter, we attract the tooth on a steady basis to avoid breaking it. If it does not come out, take one of those instruments and insert it beneath from all sides with a twisting motion, as you did initially.
If the tooth is firmly fixed or embedded, it is necessary to fill the cavity with a plug made of soft material, such as cotton wool, and pack it tightly with tweezers. Be careful not to damage the surrounding tissues while you apply pressure with the dogs (forceps). The packing must be done gradually from all sides.
Keep your effort consistent so as not to break it again, and let some of the pain remain in the patient from the first wound, for this is greater than the subsequent pains. Ensure that the forceps are made as previously described and used only as we have instructed.
It often happens that people suffer from severe pain when a tooth breaks and the root remains intact or in part. If part of the jaw bone is fractured as we have seen many times, and swelling occurs after the fracture due to drinking or eating spicy and salty food, then if bleeding occurs from the site, press something made of wool or a clean cloth on it immediately.
If the forceps do not help you, use a pair of delicate scissors whose tips are long and narrow with strong blades lest they bend when you grip them on the tooth. These are large scissors.
If the pliers do not help you, use a pair of strong pliers with narrow tips lest they bend or break. They should be made of hard iron or steel and have serrated edges that interlock securely when closing.
The tips may be designed like a tongs for added strength.

Third and Thirtieth Chapter.
In wire-tying mobile teeth with silver or gold threads.

The sixth and thirty chapter.
On the treatment of scrotal worms.
When a boil appears in the inguinal region, it may contain worms similar to those that appear externally (scrotal worms), if they are treated as described in the division, they do not heal.
If the worm is hard like lead with little sensation, do not apply iron to it. If it is red in color and its core is firm, also do not apply iron to it out of fear of bleeding. Instead, leave it until it heals. Either bind it or let it explode on its own.
If it is white in color and its core is soft, this is what needs to be cut off. The procedure for dealing with it is to check before operating whether the worm has settled or if there are any deficiencies.
When the patient is seated on a solar bed with his head against a stone, open the mouth and take an assistant between your hands. Press the tongue downwards using this instrument whose figure is shown below.

If this tool is not available, then cut it with a pair of scissors having this shape.
A lancet is sharp on one side and blunt on the other, when a boil is cut open with it, then the following boil should be cut in the same manner. After cutting, clean the area with cold water or vinegar and water.
If there is bleeding, clean it with vinegar or the leaves of onions, or something similar from herbs until the bleeding stops. Then treat it until it heals. In case other boils appear besides these two, they should be cut in the same manner as described for cutting the boils, no matter what kind they are.
The woman had a boil that had grown inside her head, causing slight pain. It seemed as if it might burst and the woman was short of breath from a narrow passageway, and she could not eat or drink water.
The boil had risen from her for several days until it came out on her nostril, so I used a lancet and pricked one of them, then pulled out a healthy piece from it.
Then I cut it where I found it from the nostril, then did the same with the boil on the other side, then I opened her mouth and held her tongue, then I pricked the lancet in the same boil, then cut a piece from it, but it only bled smoothly.
The woman's boil burst and she drank water immediately, then regained her appetite, but the boil did not recur for a long period of time, and it left behind what was cut until it healed completely, with that.
I dissolved the boil inside her head and it stopped growing, then she traveled away from that place, and I did not know what Allah had done with her after that.

In the Worm that is exposed from the bone.
As a worm can be found in the ears and the intestines, it can also appear in bones, especially if there is an injury or some kind of fracture. This occurs more frequently in patients with osteomyelitis or fractures.
And in every place where a joint exists, there is a worm that resembles the color of the body and usually does not cause pain unless it is pressed forcefully, at which point it feels like a grape or raisin. The worm is not usually found deep within the body.
It is located under the skin and moves in all directions, not towards the front or the back. Therefore, if it is not found in the joints, it should not be treated with iron. It does not typically occur in the head or neck.
Make an incision in the skin, if the worm is small then grasp it with tweezers and remove it from its source. If it is large, tie it with a ligature, cut it, then extract it. Collect the wound using stitching and treat it until it abrases (or scabs over).
Chapter one, fifty-one.
In the section of cutting the intestines that are exposed in the abdomen.
The intestines which are exposed in some people's abdomens and other organs are known as the 'fetters.' They are thin at their origin but thick at their end, they may form small outgrowths and there can be large masses as well.
A man was observed with two intestines similar to fetters. Their origin was white and thin, their ends had split and were constantly oozing fluid. They were cut and weighed approximately eight ounces in one and about six ounces in the other.
When performing the operation, if it is found that the intestine is wet and the color of the intestines is white and thin at their origin, then they should be cut with a broad blade and placed in hot coals so that much blood will flow out when they are cut.
If you find that the intestine is dark, and it contracts when cut with iron, take a strong thread made of lead and tie the affected intestine with it for a few days, then increase the tightness of the lead thread, so that the intestine does not release.
Whenever a tumor emerges and falls off without consent, if the tumor is hard at its source, it is done with some fear and trepidation, especially if it is in the abdomen; however, it may be possible to cut half of it or part of it.
Then, it is cauterized to prevent its return, and it should be treated until the wound heals, but beware of cutting tumors that resemble flesh with slight sensation and are red or bluish in appearance; for they are cancerous and will be accompanied by a mention of cancer after this.
The Second and Fiftieth Section.
On the Treatment of Hernia.
Hernia may be caused by various factors, either from the rupture of the scrotum in the abdomen and its contents protrude out elsewhere or from blood that gushes out from veins or arteries; or from wind that accumulates inside.
If it is due to the rupture of the scrotum and protrusion of the contents, its color will resemble that of a tumor, be pale without pain, and show various positions. If it is due to the protrusion of the contents, its position will be different and if you press it with your fingers it will disappear, then return and there may be swelling and increase in size when touched by water or fatigue; if it is due to moisture, it will be pale.
If you press it with your hand and neither increases nor decreases, then if it was previously blood, these signs indicate that the tumor will turn black; if it was previously flesh, the tumor will be hard and fixed in one place.
If it was previously wind, pressing it makes it slippery; and in this case, one should observe whether the tumor is connected to blood vessels of veins or arteries. In such a situation, abstaining from treatment is necessary as there is fear and risk, as you know from the chapter where you discussed tumors caused by arteries and veins.
If the tumor is connected to a nerve or tendon, one should command the patient to stop and stand still for an extended period, then learn by palpation around the entire tumor. Then command him to lean back on your chest, then press around the tumor at the location you have learned by palpation, then push the center of the tumor up with a large spoon, and tie the pressing spot with a strong cord or thin wire.
The suture of the ligature shall be tight, then it shall be opened in the middle of the tied worm above the ligature. Your little finger shall enter it and seek the abscess, if found, the ligature shall be loosened and the abscess pushed inside the abdomen. If a pus is found, draw it out with a lancet.
Cut off the protruding portion, if the wound resists or bleeds, wrap it with a soft linen cloth and return to your work, take two strong threads and insert them into the incision made around the worm as ligatures, then pass the threads through the four points on the worm.
If you want to remove the ligature, leave it until the flesh tied is healed and falls off by itself or cut it if it is painful and heals, then treat it with what is necessary to make it heal completely, if there are any hidden worms in the flesh.
If there is pus in the worm, it should be cauterized as we have said and the blood or pus found inside it should be drained, then treat the place accordingly.
Third and fifth chapter.
On cancer treatment.
We have mentioned in the section of cutting, types of cancer and the way to treat it with medicines and the warning against treating it with iron, lest it burns, and we have mentioned cancer that originates in the uterus and the warning against its treatment.
We have mentioned at the beginning that when cancer is in a place where it can be entirely excised, such as cancer in the arm or leg and similar parts capable of being removed with all its mass, it is most certainly the case for small initial cancers. However, if it has grown large, it should not be approached.
Indeed, I have not been able to cure anyone from it nor have I seen anyone before me who reached that point, and the work is done on it if we are capable as previously mentioned, namely that it advances and makes the evil more bearable then it is eliminated if it is in veins filled with blood.
Then, the evil is settled in a place that allows for work to be done on it, then it meets with the venereal cancers which are treatable, and it is sealed from all sides with skin over it, until nothing remains of its roots, and leave the blood to flow and do not cut it quickly.
Pour out and thin all the blood from the site of incision with your hand or whatever tools you have at hand, for if it resists in operation, a large amount of blood will flow from cutting veins or arteries; so apply pressure to stop the bleeding until it stops, then treat as necessary until it heals.

The eighth and fiftieth chapter.
In the treatment of retained semen in the bladder.
Retained semen in the bladder occurs due to stone, blood clot, pus or meat like substance, and similar things. If it is treated with what we have mentioned for the types of treatments described in the section on urinary stones (Al-Taqassim), then there will be no harm.
If urine has not flowed and you suspect that it is retained due to a stone in the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be made to lie on his back. Then a man should sit on his abdomen and press his stomach to his chest and hold himself.
If the stone in the neck of the bladder cannot be pushed back with the methods we mentioned, and the condition worsens for the patient, then it is necessary to use an instrument called a catheter, which looks like this:.
Make it from gold and let it be thin and sharp, like the pen of a bird in a millet reed long in about the thickness of a finger. At its tip, put a soft cotton for attraction of urine. Tie it with two threads and at one end bind a wool or linen thread well.
Insert one end of the thread into the catheter and pull it back if anything comes out from the cotton, so that it enters the tube and seals it like a cork. Then anoint the catheter with oil or soap or white lead and place the patient on a couch.
Moisten the patient's anus and apply oil or warm water, then insert the catheter into the anus up to its root. Then inflate the anus above to the opening side, then push the catheter inside it.
Until the anus is inflated, then push the catheter inside until it approaches the stool. The man urinates and the catheter is in him, then push it to reach the bladder and the patient feels that he has emptied something empty.
This instrument is made in this grade because the channel that carries urine in it is crooked, then the thread is pulled through it with some force, hence the urine follows the thread, then it is drawn out and the urine strains, and the catheter returns.
Continue doing that until the bladder empties and the discomfort subsides, [or] until the patient no longer experiences pain.

In the extraction of the stone (bladder stone).

I say that the bladder stone originating in the bladder is more prone to infections and among its signs is that urine comes out of the bladder resembling water in color.
And it appears as gravel, and he mentions its presence and spreading, and in most cases it is accompanied by itching, and often it worsens until it reaches fourteen years, and it becomes difficult for the elderly, but among the young people, it is average between this.
The larger the stone, the easier its treatment; the smaller ones, on the contrary, require more effort. When approaching the treatment, it is first necessary to aspirate the area with a syringe that draws out all the pus that may be present in the vicinity, as it may prevent the detection of the stone during examination.
Then, take the syringe and push it downwards to make the stone descend into the bladder or ascend from a higher position several times, then rest it between your hands with its head under your foot and its body in your hand to make the bladder empty completely, then examine it.
Examine it externally, if you sense a stone in the cavity, move quickly to pierce it. If it does not sink, press the forceps to hold the bladder and pierce it with the sharp finger of the left hand or with the middle finger.
If a boy is mature, enter it into his buttock and examine for the stone until it is found beneath one of your fingers. Then gently move it little by little towards the neck of the bladder, then press on it with your finger and push it out in the desired direction.

The opening should be on the same stone, and you press with your finger in the buttock to push it out obliquely so that the opening is wide outside and narrow within to facilitate the passage of the stone.
Do not exert too much pressure with the finger that is in the buttock on the stone during the opening, for it may come out easily without strain. Also be aware that some stones have angles and letters which can make their extraction difficult.
From it (the surgery), there is an extraction resembling a bladder stone, which is easily removed. If it has no angles or letters, increase the incision slightly. If it does not come out this way, it should be compressed on it firmly with a flat and hard instrument similar to a pestle.
To compress on the stone so that it does not slip away, or to enter from below it with a soft delicate instrument with a pointed tip, if it is not possible to do so on it, increase the incision slightly. If something of blood gushes out, cut it with scissors.
If there are more than one, push the larger one towards the mouth of the bladder first, then make an incision on it. Then push the smaller ones after that and do the same if there are more than two. If it is very large, know that it is not advisable to make a large incision on it because it may expose one of its parts to danger.

If your work is completed, let the incision be sealed with candle wax or oil and wait for it to harden. Then pierce it with a lancet, apply hot water or warm oil and bandage it. Do not unwrap the bandages until the third day.

The Second and Sixth Section.
In the fissure on the water pipe.

Then take two swabs, tie and secure them with a thread that is loose on this model, and make the sides that are knotted from cotton or wet thread and collect them in the suturing strap, and one side is taken to the seat towards the back.

Know that this procedure is clean and far from bleeding, and better than cutting with a knife. If you oppose the knife or if it is hot or bleeding or anything else, it is necessary to treat whatever opposes this with treatment that suits it according to what you present.

Third and Sixth Chapter.
In the Incision on the Tendon of Muscle and its Treatment.
Know that incision on this tendon is likely to lead to inflammation in most cases, hence it is left alone and safety prevails over it. However, I am reminding the work in it and its types of inflammation.
I say that inflammation occurs frequently in bodies that have an accumulation of anthrax, and this may be due to various reasons such as excessive heat causing the formation of anthrax or by a blow. The color of the inflammation is similar to the body color and it does not contain water.
The inflammation is swollen and sometimes the inflammation may be hard, its color is red and it has no sensation. It may originate from boils or from inflammation of the lymph nodes, which is known as aggravation of the inflammation.
If you squeeze it with your fingers and it should not be exposed to the bite, and as for the one that originates from inflammation of the lymph nodes, nothing aggravates it when squeezed with the fingers. This type may be incised and cut on other muscles.
It means: "Pierce the skin of the tumor (Khaisa), then push the bead upwards and extract it from the white incision, cut away the knot from the vessels, tie the vessels together, and cut the knot after it has been separated from all sides of the bead. "If the tumor is a growth of flesh in the place of adhesion, it is necessary to cut all of it and extract the bead as previously mentioned. If you have carried out your procedure and caused bleeding from the cauterized veins in the neck, use oil and wine to stop the bleeding, then treat the wound with other remedies until it heals.

The fifth and sixth sections.
In the treatment of malignant aneurysms.
This aneurysm occurs from a rupture that exposes in the extended sac on the abdomen near the armpits, from where the aneurysm migrates to one of the ovaries.
This sac may occur from a rupture, or from an extension and this type can happen for various reasons such as hitting, pressing, pulling, lifting heavy objects, and similar causes. Its symptoms are that it may occur slightly over a long period if it is due to an extension of the sac.
A boil does not occur, and the abscess is at about the same level as the puncture before the lancet has been pressed; a sign of this is if it happens from the edge of the lancet that it occurs first with a strong pain and the abscess will be different in appearance beneath the skin closely.
The abscess exits and goes out from the lancet, and it may exit with pus which is called this type of abscess and pus-discharge, and it may be accompanied by a smell; it can occur that there is mucus in the abscess and it gets blocked, thus there will also be necrosis present.
Because it occurs with a strong pain and throbbing, which is not easy to bear; the treatment for these kinds of abscesses with iron carries risk, so one must be careful not to cause it; the method of treatment is to instruct the patient to press the abscess into his own wound if he comes back.
Then, he lies on his back between your hands and raises the affected limb; then you stretch the skin above the abscess upwards and break the whole skin over it; then you make incisions in the broken skin with scissors as much as is necessary to open the abscess.
The ulcer should be as large as it can be to extract the egg, then the forceps beneath the skin are broken until the white hard scurf is exposed from all sides. Then, your thumb is inserted into what follows the egg.
Between the white hard scurf under the egg and the second scurf, and with the instrument that is behind the egg, stretch your left hand inside the skin. Meanwhile, push the white hard scurf to the top of your right hand and raise the egg along with the scurf towards the ulcer side.
The attendant commands to move the egg upward and you release the instrument that is behind it, then search with your thumb carefully so as not to find anything from the sticky matter in the white hard scurf. If you find something, push it towards the abdomen downward.
Then take a cord in which there is a thick thread that has been twisted from ten threads and insert it near the last scurf that is beneath the skin towards the ulcer side, then cut the sides of the thread until it becomes four threads. Then, it is to be connected together in a structure and the scurf that we mentioned as being beneath the skin is tied with a strong knot from two sides, then the sides of the threads are also tied with a strong knot so that nothing from the exudates that nourish them can reach it. If there is a boil that becomes hot and swells, and another rope-like thing also appears outside the first one, farther away from it than the length of two fingers, after these two ropes, discharge comes out from beneath the scab on the skin equal to the size of a bone in the finger.
If there is a boil that becomes hot and swells, and another rope-like thing also appears outside the first one, farther away from it than the length of two fingers, after these two ropes, discharge comes out from beneath the scab on the skin equal to the size of a bone in the finger. The white scab that we mentioned after cutting may be cauterized to prevent bleeding, but it is seldom necessary to do so. Leave the rope until it falls off by itself; if it sticks, press on it with hot water and hold something that absorbs heat on top of it until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with all the treatments for wounds until it heals.

The seventh and eighth sections.
In the vein which is in the right forearm.
In case the vein in the right forearm is exposed, as previously mentioned, nothing from the left side should be applied to it, and if something were to happen (i.e., if a mistake occurs), it would be easy to correct at any time.
But if the time is prolonged, the incision in the artery (i.e., the vein) will extend until the blood and pus appear in the wound, which will expose that part of the artery that is in the right forearm as previously mentioned. This is because the artery (i.e., the vein) extends, then it contracts and becomes hardened, and it stops flowing. The treatment for this is as previously described.
It can be treated with iron in this way: place the affected area on a flat surface between your hands, then make an incision in the exposed vein for about three finger widths, and tie the arteries beneath the skin.
Until the white artery (vein) that follows it is exposed, take a suture and place it on the affected part of the vein, then compress it to the depth of the abdomen, tie the two affected areas on both sides of the suture with stitches, and sew them together.

The best option in this case is because it is closest to safety.
The eighth and ninth section.
On the incision of a scarred skin.
Many people experience scarring of the skin in some cases, but not limited to the skin itself, as there is meat inside which can cause disfigurement. Therefore, anyone who wants to treat it should find out what causes it on its surface.
Cut all the scarred skin and join the two edges together, if you prefer to stitch it first, sew the thickened skin with three or four threads and pierce through them, then cut what is between the stitches.
Then treat it like other surgical wounds until the wound heals and the stitches fall out.
The ninth and tenth section.
In Al-Ikhsas (Suture).
In our law, suturing is forbidden.
This was to be avoided in my book, and it is only mentioned for two reasons: the first reason being that a physician should know its treatment if asked about it; the second reason being that we often need to use sutures on animals for our benefit.
The animals to which sutures are applied include dogs, cats and similar animals, so I say that suturing should be done with two types of stitches: one type is performed by tying knots with a heated instrument, and the other type is performed by using scissors and cutting.
Then, press it with your hand until it hardens and does not show when touched; as for suturing by cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and pull back its skin with the left hand, then tie the ligatures and sew each knot separately.
Leave a gap between the two sutures so that they do not stick together, and do not leave any thread on them except for the thin needle which is used for the stitches; this type of suture is better than the one performed by tying knots.
Since pus may remain in the female, animals gather around it, then the wound is treated until it discharges.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of women.
In the treatment of hernia, it can be found in men on two types: either it appears above the abdominal wall or within the scrotum between the testicles, resembling a woman's vagina with hair and may cause urinary leakage from the one located within the scrotum.
And as for women, it has one type: it is above the vagina like small water bladders that come out from outside resembling a man's penis and its two parts like female genitals, and the treatment of the three types.
The type in men is to cut the excessive flesh until its effect subsides, then treat it like other surgeries until it discharges. As for the second type in men that causes urinary leakage from the scrotum, there should be no treatment and no probing of the bladder.
Chapter 1 and 70.
On the removal of cysts and excessive flesh from women's vaginas.
The boil may increase its power over natural order until it becomes putrid and emits a foul smell. In some women, it can swell to the size of a male's. It may spread widely.
It is necessary to seize the boil with your hand or a pincer and cut it, refraining from cutting too deep so as not to expose blood flow.
Then treat it with surgical treatments until it drains, and as for the pus, it is meat that has grown in the womb until it fills it.
It may also come out to the outside like pus. And for this reason, it is called a purulent disease; it should be cut like a boil and treated until it drains.
The Second Chapter: Seventy.
On the Treatment of Abscesses.
Abscess is a cavity in a woman that is not pierced or if it is pierced, it is small. It may be natural, born with it, or acquired, which is due to an illness that has progressed. The acquired one may consist of pus that has grown excessively.
The lancet may be thin or thick and it can be either in the depth of the uterus, its sides, above or below, and it prevents gathering (clotting), tying, childbirth and possibly abortion, and knowing this is by observation of susceptibility.
If the cut is superficial, it should not be probed with fingers or needles. If the incision is thin and close to the edges, then make an indentation on the edges. Then place your thumb and fingers from both hands onto it.
The woman lies on her back, exposing her belly. Then the incision is made forcefully until the thin lancet is cut and the incision is opened. Then she takes a piece of thread soaked in oil and places it on the spot. The woman should gather (the area) every day to prevent the spot from being touched again.
If the lancet is thick and large, it should be cut with a broad, flat instrument that resembles paper, then if the incision is of meat, tie it with sutures and cut it off. Keep medications with you to prevent discharge other than pus, such as quinces, sheep's milk, and vinegar mixed with white egg.
Then use a catgut (intestine from a sheep or goat) that is wide enough so as not to cause quick coagulation of the wound, hold it for several days and then apply beech-tree resin (pitch). Treat with other treatments for inflammation until healed. If there is growth of flesh from another body part in the womb, it should be cut at this feature.
If it is not a cancerous tumor, the tumor that occurs in the womb does not respond to iron cauterization.
The Third and Seventieth Chapter.
On the treatment of fistulas, hemorrhoids and red ulcers that occur in women's vaginas.
As for fistulas, it is an enlargement of the openings of veins so that blood flows constantly from them. If a fistula occurs, it becomes hemorrhoids. I have mentioned its types and their symptoms earlier. Here I will explain further.
There is no treatment for them and there is no treatment that can cure them, so I say that if fistulas and hemorrhoids are deep within the womb and cannot be felt, they should not be treated with iron. If they occur in the mouth of the womb and can be felt, it is the one that should be treated.
A woman must enter a cold house, then insert the probes either by discussion or with a blunt force. She should cut it from its root when blood flows out of one of the constricting vessels for blood not from the veins.
Like the gall bladder, spleen and liver, then lift her legs to the wall, then she should be placed in cold water if bleeding continues, she should sit on a dish of hot stones and hot ashes, then take barley flour, knead it with honey and vinegar.
Press it against her abdomen, if the bleeding stops or not, then tighten the iron rods and belts without constraint, then take a cloth and immerse it in the decoction of poppy seeds or milk thistle or common mallow root with ashes drink, and insist on position.
If the worm abates, treat the position with mercury until it disappears. As for the red pus, it resembles the heads of lice, so it should be cut according to what has been described in the probes and treated until it disappears.

The fifth and seventy chapter.
On the teaching of how to treat living worms that emerge in an abnormal shape.
It is necessary for midwives to first recognize the natural shape of childbirth, and among its signs if a woman feels a strong urge to go down and breathe heavily, and there is a bulge where she has no bulge normally.
The birth will occur quickly, so know that this delivery will be natural in shape and the birth will take place on the head and the afterbirth either with it or detached from it. If you see these signs, it is necessary to squeeze the abdomen so that the child is born quickly.
If it descends onto the head, the afterbirth will descend with it and will be properly cleaned, and if this delivery occurs, it is not a natural one because the child may be born with its feet first and its hands before its head.
One hand or one foot may be born, or the head and a hand or it may emerge sideways and bend on its back or something similar to these abnormal shapes. It is necessary for those who are capable to be very careful with all of these things and avoid error.
I explain each of these shapes and how to handle them in order to guide you in this matter, if the child is born with its head, then this is a natural birth and it causes pain for the woman and labor pains become difficult for her, and if you see her strength has weakened, have her sit on a chair and instruct the women to hold her.
And [the procedure for] softening the womb with cooked hartshorn and moist poultices, then inserting the prepared fingers between them gently to break the membrane or to open it by force until the moisture within it is drained and the woman's abdomen is made to ripen until the fetus descends.
If the fetus does not descend, it is necessary to make the woman labor by applying hartshorn plaster with oil of ambergris. Then she should be ordered to strain and contract her abdomen using bellows and hold her mouth and nose until the fetus is expelled. The fetus will come out first through the hands. If this happens, it is necessary to gently guide them back into place.
If the woman does not go into labor, she should be placed on a birthing stool with her legs elevated above the ground and then the stool is shaken so that the woman does not fall off. If her hands do not enter and the fetus dies, they must be cut off and the remaining fetus retrieved.
Or tie the hands with ropes and pull them, as the fetus will come out. The fetus comes out on the legs. If the fetus comes out on the legs, it is necessary to push it upwards gently until it is straightened, then take one of the legs and gently guide it along.
If it comes out into the fingers, order her to wash and anoint it with alum, for it will come out. If it does not come out as we have described, and the fetus is slightly expelled bit by bit until it becomes in its natural shape, it will come out smoothly when that happens. In this case, prevent everything we have described.
A fracture of the finger or thumb, a burn on the shin and anointing with oil should be treated by dissolving camphor and striking all around it forcefully. Then put her on her back and lower her abdomen. After that, let her sit in warm water until the pain subsides.
If you suspect that the fetus is lying bottom-up, make a small incision near its navel and let it heal. When the incision heals, hold the mother on a chair, then press and compress it. Close both her nostrils, pinch her nose shut and make an incision in her lower abdomen with a sharp instrument. This will cause the fetus to be expelled from her within an hour. The expulsion of the fetus will occur through its back and legs.
If it is in this position, insert your fingers gently and gradually. The woman will then squat and pull her legs apart while she lies down on a bed, with her hands resting on the ground. Then, make a small incision on her abdomen. Then, remove the amniotic sac from her legs until it is located at the bottom. If the fetus does not come out, grasp both of her legs and move them forcefully. Make a small incision above the pubic bone only enough for the fetus to ascend. Then, the one who is skilled should enter with their hand and gently manipulate the fetus.
The woman must expel the fetus, and its exit may be difficult due to resistance. If you cannot grab it, make the woman sit up straight and walk. If she cannot walk, she should rest.
Massage the patient's abdomen and shake her sides violently, then apply the leech described in the games if it can be obtained. Place it on a chair, treat her in the hand and set the fetus back to its natural shape. Apply pressure to the woman and order her to bear down until it comes out.
The delivery of the child face up, with his head towards the mother's chest. It is recommended that those who are capable grasp the child's head and slowly turn it, while adjusting its position when necessary. When it aligns, hold it with the ointment and games we described earlier.
After making the woman move slightly, if she does so, place her on a chair and order her to lean towards the right side. Then make her bear down and apply pressure with your fingers; the child will be born in breech position.
If the water breaks from the uterus in this manner and there is mucus, tear the mucus with your fingernail until it stops flowing, grasp the face of the child and its neck. Cut the nuchal cord without causing strangulation so that the child does not choke and die. Then push the child inside until it is in the correct position.
A woman must leech herself several times, for it is easy to evacuate, many boils or pimples will come out. Know that boils frequently produce offspring; they may produce three or four, but this usually happens in the abscess. As for five, it is something unnatural and the embryos do not live.
Encircle them and if they multiply, let it be with a single blister. They will split with a sharp probe between them, each one being enclosed in its own sheath, and just as a baby is naturally born easily, so too will the boils emerge in a natural way, though their emergence may be painful as described earlier.
If some of them are difficult to deliver and they become what we have described as unnatural forms, treat them as we have described earlier, so that they may be gentle and do what they can with skill and convert into any shape suitable for healing, leading to safety.
Mentioned is what can be found in the womb as boils that fall down; they may form singly, in pairs, trios, quartets, quintuplets, sextuplets and more than ten. I have heard of a woman who passed seven and another who passed fifteen, all of them being boil-like structures.
Esteemed and knowledgeable [person], this should all be in the science of cauterization, as there may be such incidents one day which require what is appropriate for it.
The sixth and seventieth chapter.
On the extraction of the stillborn child.
If you treat the stillborn child as described in the section on treatment, but it does not come out and the situation requires manual intervention, then if the woman is healthy and has no symptoms that could cause harm to her, she should lie down on her back.
The head should be situated lower, the neck elevated twice and its keeper adjusts it from either side or ties it to the bed so that the body does not draw it upon completion of the pregnancy.
Then, the mouth of her womb is turned with moist cotton swabs, with forceps and a canula, then the capable hand smears these materials on her abdomen and the forceps, then she enters into the womb accompanied by them, and seeks a place to anchor the fetal hooks in it. The suitable positions for this are.
If the fetus is positioned head down, anchor the fetal hooks in one of its eyes or ears or mouth or navel or back or near the breech or under the shoulders.
If it is positioned on its feet, in the breech position, the fetal hook should be grasped with the right hand and placed between the fingers of the left hand, then the left hand enters along with it and anchors the fetal hook in one of the positions mentioned earlier.
Continue until you reach something empty, then anchor another or third fetal hook in her cervix to balance the pull and not direct it towards one side. Then move steadily without the pull being only upwards, but moving towards all sides.
It is not easy to extract as in tooth extraction during gum swelling. It is necessary, between that, to pack the cavity with a bandage; if one side of it is blocked, it is necessary to anoint some fingers with oil and enter them from there so as to turn what is blocked. If any infant comes out, the forceps are moved to other places.
It is not done easily, until all the infants are extracted. If a hand comes out before another and it cannot be returned due to its swelling, then it is necessary to break it; afterwards, it should be drawn back until all of them come out in pieces.
Either in the wrist or in the ankle, and this must be done in both hands and feet; if the head of the infant is large and there is pressure upon its exit, or if there is water collected in its head, then it is necessary to enter between the fingers with a probe.
Crush its head so that the water comes out or press it with the instrument called the forceps, which is depicted alongside other instruments in the illustration that follows.
Likewise, this is done if the infant is large-headed. It is necessary to crush its skull or press it with the forceps as previously mentioned; then, the bones are extracted with forceps, and when the head comes out and there is pressure during extraction, it should be crushed until the fluid in the chest is released.
If the chest does not join together, and it does not open by itself, then cut as much as you can. If it is below the abdomen or there is pus in it, it is necessary to pack it until the moisture drains out from it.
If the fetus is on the mother's thigh, then drawing it out is easy and you will straighten it into the womb. If pressure is felt near the abdomen or chest, it is necessary to draw it out with a hook that you have shaped with your hand and pierce the abdomen or chest until the content drains out from them.
When all the limbs are extracted and the head is withdrawn, place it in the left hand. If the womb is open, insert the left hand into its neck and grasp the head with your fingers. Then insert a cannula or two cannulas into it and pull it by them.
If the womb is tightly closed with a hot, narrow opening, do not push on it. Instead, use cold, damp objects and apply them and sit in warm water and soak it.
And if the fetus is on the side, it can be moved. Do not perform what we mentioned for a living fetus unless it cannot be moved in which case it should be cut and removed. It is necessary that nothing remains of the placenta inside the womb. If your treatment is finished, use what we have mentioned to treat hot, painful abscesses that occur in the womb.
If a flow of blood appears, let it descend into tight water and apply all treatments. I have seen a woman who had given birth, the baby died inside her, then she tied another knot on it.
Then the second baby also died, and after a long time, she had a swelling and fever in her examination, and it inflated until it opened and released pus. I called her for treatment, so I treated her for a long time, but the wound did not heal. She placed some strong adhesive plasters on it.
A bone came out from the place, then she stayed for some days, and another bone came out. She was amazed that her belly had no bones in it because the baby was dead. She thought that the bones were of the dead baby. So, she explored the wound and took out many bones from the head of the baby.
I did not stop following that until she took out many bones from her, and the woman was in good health, and it had been leaking pus easily for a long time. I have brought this rare case to you here.
For there is knowledge and help for the physician in making treatment with his hands.

The eighth and seventy-seventh section.
On the extraction of a tumor.
If the tumor is firmly attached after expiration, it is necessary to order the assistant to hold herself then pinch her with forceps and press hard on her mouth and nose so that if it comes out with this or otherwise take a sheet:.
And pierce the cover and put in it ointments for the mouth of the uterus such as fodens, sadeh, shabt, babunj, sheikh, salicha, qantourioun, all these drugs or some of them, immerse them in water and carry them to the fire then place a copper tube on the opening of the cover of the sheet and the other side in the mouth of the uterus.
Hold it (the patient) until the hot irons reach the navel, then squeeze as previously stated; for the pus will come out quickly. If, after this treatment, it does not come out, command the one who can do so to rub his left hand in sheep fat or ointment of bruises.
Then insert it (the probe) into the navel and search for the pus; if it strikes it, grasp it and draw it out little by little until it comes out. If it is tightly attached in the depth of the navel, place your hand as we have described until you find the pus, then gently pull it out.
In order not to let the navel fall during strong pulling, it is better to move it towards the sides, right and left, then gradually increase the pulling force; for it will respond when doing so and free itself from adhesion. If there is pus in the navel, we have previously described the treatment as squeezing and the method of pressure and cauterization.
If it does not come out with all the treatments we have previously described, then you may try to apply force on it for re-pulling; but it is better to tie what comes out from it to the navel of the woman and then squeeze it with four fingers. For it will soften after a few days.
The incision heals and comes out except that if it decomposes, then a foul smell rises from it to the body and the head and it hurts. Therefore, it is necessary to use agreeable smoke.

The Ninth and Seventieth Chapter.
On the Treatment of Non-Pierced Warts.
If many children have warts that are not pierced, it is advisable for the person who is able to pierce them with a sharp awl and if not, then tie it tightly with a hard thread and be careful not to touch the nerves.
Then, soak it in a solution and oil, then treat it with a poultice until it heals. If you fear that it may break open, place a lead tube over the piercing for several days and remove it when the child wants to heal.
The rupture of the scrotum can also be caused by injury or abscess. It should be drained first, then treated as described earlier.
Chapter twenty.
Treatment of abscesses that occur in the lower region.
Abscesses that occur in the lower region are to be opened and drained, which happens close to or outside the scrotum, or within one of its sides. The abscess may be singular or multiple.
If the abscess is swollen, it should be opened and pus of a watery white or thin yellow color will flow out of it. Such abscesses may drain into the spermatic vessels or the bladder and not be draining. The draining abscesses can be recognized by the discharge of pus and gas when a probe is inserted.
If pus has come out of it, and there are openings from it into the intestine, to the bladder and to the urethra, or into the scrotum, and what is known as a hernia into the saddle [area], such cases should be treated.
If your little finger gets trapped in the saddle and a thin wire of brass or iron enters the hernia, but it is not within the hernia, then treat it. But if there is a protrusion [of the hernia], insert a thin wire of lead or horse hair into it.
Until you feel the wire or the hair in your little finger, if you do not feel any pain or discomfort and nothing from the hernia protrudes or emits wind, pus, or foul smell as we said, then it is not a hernia. In this case, proceed with treatment.
If the hernia is opening into the bladder or urethra, a sign of it is the discharge of urine from it and its refusal to be treated with medication. As for when the hernia opens into the scrotum or groin, a sign of this is the arrival of the wire there.
If it does not contain a joint to the bone, and there is a wound near its side and continuous discharge from it, and it does not heal, there is no treatment for it and it should not be tampered with. These open wounds are all excluded from the cauterization of the cauterizer.
Treatment of such wounds is futile for those who foolishly attempt to treat them, and as for those that are not open or not continuous, the cauterization by iron is suitable for them according to my description and what I have tried, and it means to apply pressure between your fingers on its surface.
The person who is causing the bleeding should be raised up and his arm pushed towards the abdomen, then a copper or lead wire should be inserted until it reaches the joint if there is one in the finger, then feel around the area like a chair. If you sense the end of the wire, insert your thumb into the area.
If you sense the wire in your thumb, it has emerged by itself without feeling between your thumb and it with a probe or flesh, then be assured that it is open and there is no need for cauterization as we mentioned earlier.
They said that it makes bleeding stop in some people during childbirth, and the treatment which is beneficial for this is to apply a fine cupping glass according to the size of the nar (womb), as it is introduced into the nar up to its seat, then it is withdrawn twice or thrice.
They said that all those excess, hardened meats resembling bird's intestines which have been burned should be treated by fatting ointment in oil, until the burnt meat comes out, then it is treated with salves containing alum, so that it stops bleeding.
Unless another treatment is applied, it will not stop bleeding permanently; if the cord was introduced and did not reach the fingertip in the seat of the uterus and there was a thick covering of meat or membrane between them, and you see the uterus protruding above the skin surface, then the skin is torn from the beginning of the uterus. You tear the cord along with the skin in the uterus until the tearing reaches where the end of the cord is and it separates, and the cord falls off, then you remove the hardened meats resembling bird's intestines and there remains nothing from it.
Then treat it with caustic lime until it blisters. If the bleeding persists and there is a swelling both in your condition and in the affected area, cut away that flesh; it is best to apply fire or a sharp cautery because burning helps to coagulate the excessive flesh.
Cut away the blood and drain the fluids, then treat it with oil of roses or powdered sulfur in oil until the area is clean and the burned flesh comes out in the cleaning process. After that, treat the wound with sharp cautery for tough meat.
This is the medicine that clears and stops bleeding, so if it stops then it has been cured and there will be no relapse. If the nar has reached a deep wound below the surface of the body, insert your finger into the wound and probe it with it.
If you feel a cord and there is a covering between it and you, whether it is flesh or some other substance and it is near the opening, then do not work on it except by means of patience and prayer, and this is because there are three possible ways to deal with it: either to press it until it comes out, or to use an emetic such as vinegar, or to incise it and let the pus drain.
If it is to be cut until it reaches its hollow, so that the fillet and treatment can be performed close by without cutting into the surrounding muscles, then, due to its proximity, pus may come out unintentionally. Then treat it as previously mentioned, perhaps it will heal as we said.
If it is to perform that incision and then cut it close to the seat as previously mentioned, either with a string or another sharp tool, then clean all the contaminated meat within the wound as much as possible by cutting.
Then ram the wound edges and the upper jaw until it is closed, leaving the nostrils open within the seat. This makes it less noticeable, and the nose may break on this feature.
If you insert the string into the nose and it is near the seat on the side of the body with the skin and the edge of the seat, then take a string pierced at its end like the hook of an awl in this image:.
Place a loose thread of five or about that number in it, then insert the string through the nose until it reaches its hollow. If it is an opening in the seat from inside near it.
Draw the thread from that hole by inserting your finger into the wound and pulling out one side of the thread, then gather both ends together, tighten them, and leave it for a day or two. Whenever the thread is cut in the flesh, tighten it firmly until that piece of meat between the threads is severed and falls off, then treat the wound until it heals and closes up.
If the nose of the Nasara (non-Muslims) is not open, open it as much as possible without causing damage to the bone structure. Then proceed as previously described until it heals and closes up.
