That is because it protrudes inside and outside, towards front and back, and it mostly protrudes more towards the inside than towards the front or back. A sign of a disc protrusion towards the inside is that if you feel for the patient's pulse on the correct side, it will be longer.
The hernia is more painful than the correct position, and it is not possible for the patient to raise his leg among the Arabs (i.e., Bedouins), and it is obvious that the place where the big toe is pointing towards is the location.
A sign of a fracture that exposes to the outside is different from these symptoms, and a sign of a fracture that exposes to the front is that it spreads the leg completely, but it does not shorten it unless there is pain in the hernia, and walking is impossible for him at this location towards the front.
The wound is stopped and the urine is pressed out, and when walking it becomes discharged at the posterior part. The sign of one who exposes his buttock to such a thing is that he does not widen the saddle nor can he bend it before bending the buttocks, and his gait is also shorter than the others.
The buttocks are contracted, and the head of the penis is located at the site of the injury. As for the kinds of this affliction, if this fistula has been affecting its owner for a long time without him attempting to cure it, there is no treatment for the abscess.
It is not advisable to expose oneself to it, and as for the one who has been fistulated in any of the four openings of the anus, he must wash the affected area well, move it gently inward and outward until softened.
He returned and did not require any other treatment, but if he does not return in this way, it is necessary to summon a strong servant with his hands or ropes that are tied on his buttocks above the saddle and a second servant pulls him from below.
The hand should enter from beneath the navel, then it shall be tightened by thin thread on the root of the finger and an assistant holds one end of the thread. It may extend either from the front side to the back or from the rear to the chest.
All of them shall be drawn out in one movement until the object rises from the earth and remains suspended, for this type of extraction is a shared characteristic among the four types. If the object returns as we have said or otherwise, it is necessary for each type to use the treatment that was specifically mentioned.
If the object is inside, it should be pulled out on its correct side. Then a cord should be tied around the root of the finger between the tip and the navel area.
Then the cord should be pulled up from the navel side to the upper body towards the back, and an assistant holds it firmly with his hands. He grasps the thickened part of the finger with his hand and pulls out the object forcefully. It will return to its original position.
This type is easier than other methods of treatment that involve this joint, but if it is difficult for you and you do not need to perform this type of treatment, then all the limbs of the object should be tied with thin cords at the elbows and knees.
After each of them (the fingers), there should be a span of four fingers, and the index finger (small) should be extended more than the other one by two fingers' width. Then, he (the patient) ties the affected (index finger) to a wooden peg that is in the house, and there should be two arm lengths after it on the ground.
Then, he commands a strong boy to hold the head of the finger and tie it with the affected (index finger). Another boy then holds the finger being tied and pushes it forcefully. The separation (between the fingers) returns quickly to its place, unless the jaw moves outwards.
The affected (index finger) should be placed on the window sill as previously described in the case of the club foot, and the rope should be tied tightly around it and to its joint and chest. Then, two wooden pieces are placed under his legs and one at his head, and a large piece of wood is placed in the middle of the window sill as a support.
A moist warm poultice should be placed on it so as not to harm the affected (index finger), and a piece of wood should be placed between his fingers to prevent it from moving downwards during the procedure, then each attendant should go to their side and the physician straightens the ropes if he responds to the treatment.
Except that it is placed upon him, and it is tied on what we mentioned in the cavity; except that it is necessary that the injury be on his correct side. And if the extraction is towards the front, it is necessary that the finger be withdrawn one time, and he is described thus with his eye on the thumb.
The physician places his left hand on the injured finger, then presses it with the other hand while applying constant pressure towards the bottom (palm side) of the finger. If extraction is towards the back, it should not be pulled downward.
It should be raised above the ground but it is necessary that it be secured on something hard, also it should be from both its tip and root according to what we mentioned of the injury on the thumb. And it is closed (bound) with ties.
According to what we said, the splinter should be applied with a knife on the spot where it has exited. If the tip of the finger has completely returned, its sign will not escape your notice and is indicated by the finger being withdrawn (straightened).
If you see them both in line and the finger is contracted but not constricted, know that it has returned to its normal state. In this case, tie the fingers together and apply a thick bandage tightly so that the finger does not move to any of the directions.
The patient must be immobilized. The sutures and bindings shall be loosened after three or four days, then the wound shall be sewn with the other [side], if you see both in good condition, know that the fracture has set, release the immobilizer and let the patient walk, but if you see anything of swelling.
Return and bind it again as you did before, then leave it for three days, then open it up and let him walk on it for as long as necessary until it heals, God willing.
The second and third sections.
Treatment of fractures.
A fracture occurs in three directions, internally, externally, and downwards, meaning towards the back and not towards the front of the buttock, and a sign of a fracture is that the patient orders the immobilizer to hold his leg onto the side of the boot.
If he does not hold his leg onto the side of the boot, then know that the fracture is not displaced, force all sides of the fracture to make him sit down and if he can do so, let him sit with his assistant behind him to support him and guide him slightly from behind, then you sit on his feet.
Place the posterior (back) of your hand upon your face, and let the leg of the scalpel be between your fingers. Then grasp it with your fingers and interlock them on the handle. After that, draw it strongly to the side of the handle with your fist and another assistant shall push the leg until the handle returns to its place.
The sign that it has returned is when the tip of the scalpel touches the bone, then press and attach the tip to the bone, then bind them together with three ligatures for three or four days, then release them. It shall not be used except by little walking for a few days until it heals.
If it is difficult for you to return it as we have described, then apply strong traction with the ligatures that we have previously mentioned in the treatment of the dislocation.
The third and thirty-third chapter.
On the treatment of the fracture of the skull.
The skull fracture may easily heal by itself or it may break completely and be displaced either internally or externally, and the sign of a fracture is that you see the skull bulging on the side to which it has been displaced.
As for the treatment of a simple healing, it is easy to reduce by hand and hold it until it returns, and as for the treatment if it breaks completely, the patient should sit upright and a strong assistant holds him from behind his back in the middle.
Then grasp your right hand at the top of its foot, and your left hand at the bottom of its foot in the position of the instep. Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then with your left hand twice, then stretch it with your left hand, push the heel of the foot with your right hand towards the big toe without force.
Then make the same action as described, then push the heel towards the big toe in the third pull and you are pulling at the instep. If it returns in one or two attempts with this characteristic and you see the foot flat, otherwise correct the work on it because it will return.
If it is prevented from returning as described, then place the heel on the ground and secure it firmly to the ground with a strong pressure between his feet so that it does not harm the heel, then the servant holds the foot.
Then the last servant of the man pulls him either by hand or by a rope tied around his neck, then each servant pulls in opposite directions and the body is held up between the feet of the heel to prevent it from falling during the stretching, then the doctor straightens the leg with his hands.
The last servant holds the correct vein towards the lower part; then, when the ligature returns quickly, if it returns and clarifies its correctness to you, take hold of the ligature and the knot and tighten it with thongs and thread, and apply your foot to the thongs downward. It is necessary that you be cautious from the blow that will be above the buttock from behind.
Do not let the thong be too tight, so as not to injure it, then leave it for a couple or three days if it swells. If the thong becomes swollen, tighten it, then release it on the third or fourth day, and prevent the patient from walking for forty days.
If the patient walks before this period, it will not be safe for the ligature to hold and it will burst or rot, and treatment after that will not be accepted. If he limps with a hot swelling, it is necessary to use what has been described in another place of our treatise and refrain from walking until it subsides.
Fourth and Thirtieth Chapter.
Treatment of Ligature of Finger Veins in the Male.
It is necessary to fill up the wound left by ligature with a soft substance other than pus, and this is not difficult but easy; if the ligature is in some part of the foot's sole, it is necessary that the patient put his foot on a level place on the ground.
"And on a bone, and he stands like a mannequin, then you position your foot on the end of the bone, and press it with force until it returns and you see that it has been broken but does not appear in the position.
"Then put a splint under the foot bone so that it takes hold of the entire foot with two ends, then press it firmly and accurately for three days, then dissolve it and remove it from walking for several days until it hardens and ensures the return, if God wills.
"Chapter Fifty-Third
"In types of fractures that occur with injury or breakage, or both together.
"When such things occur and treatment is applied, it often ends in death.
"Therefore, it should not be attempted to treat such cases except by a skilled craftsman with long experience, sharp eyesight, good judgment, no deformity or dislocation, and the use of medicines that soothe inflammation alone, and he must be patient.
"O Allah, may you grant us safety from pain with mild sickness and give us some hope in it before the inflammation occurs.
If a limb returns as desired, apply the treatment that inhabits the hot abscesses and heals wounds with appropriate cauterization. If the fracture occurs along with a bone crack and free shards take place, extract them. Equivalent to what we mentioned in simple diseases, it proceeds in the cases presented.
Exert your effort and be cautious of entering the path of error on what you face, and follow my advice for that is best for you and submits to your presentation if God wills it.
